2172         /**
2173          * Returns a ClassDefiner that creates a {@code Class} object of a hidden class
2174          * from the given bytes.  No package name check on the given name.
2175          *
2176          * @param name    fully-qualified name that specifies the prefix of the hidden class
2177          * @param bytes   class bytes
2178          * @return ClassDefiner that defines a hidden class of the given bytes.
2179          */
2180         ClassDefiner makeHiddenClassDefiner(String name, byte[] bytes) {
2181             // skip name and access flags validation
2182             return makeHiddenClassDefiner(ClassFile.newInstanceNoCheck(name, bytes), Set.of(), false);
2183         }
2184 
2185         /**
2186          * Returns a ClassDefiner that creates a {@code Class} object of a hidden class
2187          * from the given class file and options.
2188          *
2189          * @param cf ClassFile
2190          * @param options class options
2191          * @param accessVmAnnotations true to give the hidden class access to VM annotations
2192          */
2193         private ClassDefiner makeHiddenClassDefiner(ClassFile cf,
2194                                                     Set<ClassOption> options,
2195                                                     boolean accessVmAnnotations) {
2196             int flags = HIDDEN_CLASS | ClassOption.optionsToFlag(options);
2197             if (accessVmAnnotations | VM.isSystemDomainLoader(lookupClass.getClassLoader())) {
2198                 // jdk.internal.vm.annotations are permitted for classes
2199                 // defined to boot loader and platform loader
2200                 flags |= ACCESS_VM_ANNOTATIONS;
2201             }
2202 
2203             return new ClassDefiner(this, cf, flags);
2204         }
2205 
2206         static class ClassDefiner {
2207             private final Lookup lookup;
2208             private final String name;
2209             private final byte[] bytes;
2210             private final int classFlags;
2211 
2212             private ClassDefiner(Lookup lookup, ClassFile cf, int flags) {
2213                 assert ((flags & HIDDEN_CLASS) != 0 || (flags & STRONG_LOADER_LINK) == STRONG_LOADER_LINK);
2214                 this.lookup = lookup;
2215                 this.bytes = cf.bytes;
2216                 this.name = cf.name;
2217                 this.classFlags = flags;
2218             }
2219 
2220             String className() {
2221                 return name;
2222             }
2223 
2224             Class<?> defineClass(boolean initialize) {
2225                 return defineClass(initialize, null);
2226             }
2227 
2228             Lookup defineClassAsLookup(boolean initialize) {
2229                 Class<?> c = defineClass(initialize, null);
2230                 return new Lookup(c, null, FULL_POWER_MODES);
2231             }
2232 
2233             /**
2234              * Defines the class of the given bytes and the given classData.
2235              * If {@code initialize} parameter is true, then the class will be initialized.
2236              *
2237              * @param initialize true if the class to be initialized
2238              * @param classData classData or null
2239              * @return the class
2240              *
2241              * @throws LinkageError linkage error
2242              */
2243             Class<?> defineClass(boolean initialize, Object classData) {
2244                 Class<?> lookupClass = lookup.lookupClass();
2245                 ClassLoader loader = lookupClass.getClassLoader();
2246                 ProtectionDomain pd = (loader != null) ? lookup.lookupClassProtectionDomain() : null;
2247                 Class<?> c = SharedSecrets.getJavaLangAccess()
2248                         .defineClass(loader, lookupClass, name, bytes, pd, initialize, classFlags, classData);
2249                 assert !isNestmate() || c.getNestHost() == lookupClass.getNestHost();
2250                 return c;
2251             }
2252 
2253             Lookup defineClassAsLookup(boolean initialize, Object classData) {
2254                 // initialize must be true if classData is non-null
2255                 assert classData == null || initialize == true;
2256                 Class<?> c = defineClass(initialize, classData);
2257                 return new Lookup(c, null, FULL_POWER_MODES);
2258             }
2259 
2260             private boolean isNestmate() {
2261                 return (classFlags & NESTMATE_CLASS) != 0;
2262             }
2263         }
2264 
2265         private ProtectionDomain lookupClassProtectionDomain() {
2266             ProtectionDomain pd = cachedProtectionDomain;
2267             if (pd == null) {
2268                 cachedProtectionDomain = pd = SharedSecrets.getJavaLangAccess().protectionDomain(lookupClass);
2269             }
2270             return pd;
2271         }
2272 
2273         // cached protection domain
2274         private volatile ProtectionDomain cachedProtectionDomain;
2275 
2276         // Make sure outer class is initialized first.
2277         static { IMPL_NAMES.getClass(); }
2278 
2279         /** Package-private version of lookup which is trusted. */
2280         static final Lookup IMPL_LOOKUP = new Lookup(Object.class, null, TRUSTED);
2281 
2282         /** Version of lookup which is trusted minimally.
2283          *  It can only be used to create method handles to publicly accessible
2284          *  members in packages that are exported unconditionally.
2285          */
2286         static final Lookup PUBLIC_LOOKUP = new Lookup(Object.class, null, UNCONDITIONAL);
2287 
2288         private static void checkUnprivilegedlookupClass(Class<?> lookupClass) {
2289             String name = lookupClass.getName();
2290             if (name.startsWith("java.lang.invoke."))
2291                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal lookupClass: "+lookupClass);
2292         }
2293 
2294         /**
2295          * Displays the name of the class from which lookups are to be made,
2296          * followed by "/" and the name of the {@linkplain #previousLookupClass()
2297          * previous lookup class} if present.
2298          * (The name is the one reported by {@link java.lang.Class#getName() Class.getName}.)
2299          * If there are restrictions on the access permitted to this lookup,
2300          * this is indicated by adding a suffix to the class name, consisting
2301          * of a slash and a keyword.  The keyword represents the strongest
2302          * allowed access, and is chosen as follows:
2303          * <ul>
2304          * <li>If no access is allowed, the suffix is "/noaccess".
2305          * <li>If only unconditional access is allowed, the suffix is "/publicLookup".
2306          * <li>If only public access to types in exported packages is allowed, the suffix is "/public".
2307          * <li>If only public and module access are allowed, the suffix is "/module".
2308          * <li>If public and package access are allowed, the suffix is "/package".
2309          * <li>If public, package, and private access are allowed, the suffix is "/private".
2310          * </ul>
2311          * If none of the above cases apply, it is the case that full access
2312          * (public, module, package, private, and protected) is allowed.
2313          * In this case, no suffix is added.
2314          * This is true only of an object obtained originally from
2315          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#lookup MethodHandles.lookup}.
2316          * Objects created by {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.Lookup#in Lookup.in}
2317          * always have restricted access, and will display a suffix.
2318          * <p>
2319          * (It may seem strange that protected access should be
2320          * stronger than private access.  Viewed independently from
2321          * package access, protected access is the first to be lost,
2322          * because it requires a direct subclass relationship between
2323          * caller and callee.)
2324          * @see #in
2325          *
2326          * @revised 9
2327          * @spec JPMS
2328          */
2329         @Override
2330         public String toString() {
2331             String cname = lookupClass.getName();
2332             if (prevLookupClass != null)
2333                 cname += "/" + prevLookupClass.getName();
2334             switch (allowedModes) {
2335             case 0:  // no privileges
2336                 return cname + "/noaccess";
2337             case UNCONDITIONAL:
2338                 return cname + "/publicLookup";
2339             case PUBLIC:
2340                 return cname + "/public";
2341             case PUBLIC|MODULE:
2342                 return cname + "/module";
2343             case PUBLIC|PACKAGE:
2344             case PUBLIC|MODULE|PACKAGE:
2345                 return cname + "/package";
2346             case FULL_POWER_MODES & (~PROTECTED):
2347             case FULL_POWER_MODES & ~(PROTECTED|MODULE):
2348                 return cname + "/private";
2349             case FULL_POWER_MODES:
2350             case FULL_POWER_MODES & (~MODULE):
2351                 return cname;
2352             case TRUSTED:
2353                 return "/trusted";  // internal only; not exported
2354             default:  // Should not happen, but it's a bitfield...
2355                 cname = cname + "/" + Integer.toHexString(allowedModes);
2356                 assert(false) : cname;
2357                 return cname;
2358             }
2359         }
2360 
2361         /**
2362          * Produces a method handle for a static method.
2363          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method.
2364          * (Since static methods do not take receivers, there is no
2365          * additional receiver argument inserted into the method handle type,
2366          * as there would be with {@link #findVirtual findVirtual} or {@link #findSpecial findSpecial}.)
2367          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2368          * <p>
2369          * The returned method handle will have
2370          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2371          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2372          * <p>
2373          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the method's class will
2374          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2375          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2376          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2377 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2378 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2379 ...
2380 MethodHandle MH_asList = publicLookup().findStatic(Arrays.class,
2381   "asList", methodType(List.class, Object[].class));
2382 assertEquals("[x, y]", MH_asList.invoke("x", "y").toString());
2383          * }</pre></blockquote>
2384          * @param refc the class from which the method is accessed
2385          * @param name the name of the method
2386          * @param type the type of the method
2387          * @return the desired method handle
2388          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2389          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2390          *                                or if the method is not {@code static},
2391          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2392          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2393          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2394          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2395          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2396          */
2397         public MethodHandle findStatic(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2398             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(REF_invokeStatic, refc, name, type);
2399             // resolveOrFail could return a non-static <init> method if present
2400             // detect and throw NSME before producing a MethodHandle
2401             if (!method.isStatic() && name.equals("<init>")) {
2402                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("illegal method name: " + name);
2403             }
2404 
2405             return getDirectMethod(REF_invokeStatic, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2406         }
2407 
2408         /**
2409          * Produces a method handle for a virtual method.
2410          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2411          * with the receiver type (usually {@code refc}) prepended.
2412          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2413          * <p>
2414          * When called, the handle will treat the first argument as a receiver
2415          * and, for non-private methods, dispatch on the receiver's type to determine which method
2416          * implementation to enter.
2417          * For private methods the named method in {@code refc} will be invoked on the receiver.
2418          * (The dispatching action is identical with that performed by an
2419          * {@code invokevirtual} or {@code invokeinterface} instruction.)
2420          * <p>
2421          * The first argument will be of type {@code refc} if the lookup
2422          * class has full privileges to access the member.  Otherwise
2423          * the member must be {@code protected} and the first argument
2424          * will be restricted in type to the lookup class.
2425          * <p>
2426          * The returned method handle will have
2427          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2428          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2429          * <p>
2430          * Because of the general <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">equivalence</a> between {@code invokevirtual}
2431          * instructions and method handles produced by {@code findVirtual},
2432          * if the class is {@code MethodHandle} and the name string is
2433          * {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke}, the resulting
2434          * method handle is equivalent to one produced by
2435          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#exactInvoker MethodHandles.exactInvoker} or
2436          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#invoker MethodHandles.invoker}
2437          * with the same {@code type} argument.
2438          * <p>
2439          * If the class is {@code VarHandle} and the name string corresponds to
2440          * the name of a signature-polymorphic access mode method, the resulting
2441          * method handle is equivalent to one produced by
2442          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#varHandleInvoker} with
2443          * the access mode corresponding to the name string and with the same
2444          * {@code type} arguments.
2445          * <p>
2446          * <b>Example:</b>
2447          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2448 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2449 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2450 ...
2451 MethodHandle MH_concat = publicLookup().findVirtual(String.class,
2452   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
2453 MethodHandle MH_hashCode = publicLookup().findVirtual(Object.class,
2454   "hashCode", methodType(int.class));
2455 MethodHandle MH_hashCode_String = publicLookup().findVirtual(String.class,
2456   "hashCode", methodType(int.class));
2457 assertEquals("xy", (String) MH_concat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
2458 assertEquals("xy".hashCode(), (int) MH_hashCode.invokeExact((Object)"xy"));
2459 assertEquals("xy".hashCode(), (int) MH_hashCode_String.invokeExact("xy"));
2460 // interface method:
2461 MethodHandle MH_subSequence = publicLookup().findVirtual(CharSequence.class,
2462   "subSequence", methodType(CharSequence.class, int.class, int.class));
2463 assertEquals("def", MH_subSequence.invoke("abcdefghi", 3, 6).toString());
2464 // constructor "internal method" must be accessed differently:
2465 MethodType MT_newString = methodType(void.class); //()V for new String()
2466 try { assertEquals("impossible", lookup()
2467         .findVirtual(String.class, "<init>", MT_newString));
2468  } catch (NoSuchMethodException ex) { } // OK
2469 MethodHandle MH_newString = publicLookup()
2470   .findConstructor(String.class, MT_newString);
2471 assertEquals("", (String) MH_newString.invokeExact());
2472          * }</pre></blockquote>
2473          *
2474          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2475          * @param name the name of the method
2476          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
2477          * @return the desired method handle
2478          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2479          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2480          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
2481          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2482          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2483          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2484          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2485          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2486          */
2487         public MethodHandle findVirtual(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2488             if (refc == MethodHandle.class) {
2489                 MethodHandle mh = findVirtualForMH(name, type);
2490                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
2491             } else if (refc == VarHandle.class) {
2492                 MethodHandle mh = findVirtualForVH(name, type);
2493                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
2494             }
2495             byte refKind = (refc.isInterface() ? REF_invokeInterface : REF_invokeVirtual);
2496             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(refKind, refc, name, type);
2497             return getDirectMethod(refKind, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2498         }
2499         private MethodHandle findVirtualForMH(String name, MethodType type) {
2500             // these names require special lookups because of the implicit MethodType argument
2501             if ("invoke".equals(name))
2502                 return invoker(type);
2503             if ("invokeExact".equals(name))
2504                 return exactInvoker(type);
2505             assert(!MemberName.isMethodHandleInvokeName(name));
2506             return null;
2507         }
2508         private MethodHandle findVirtualForVH(String name, MethodType type) {
2509             try {
2510                 return varHandleInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode.valueFromMethodName(name), type);
2511             } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
2512                 return null;
2513             }
2514         }
2515 
2516         /**
2517          * Produces a method handle which creates an object and initializes it, using
2518          * the constructor of the specified type.
2519          * The parameter types of the method handle will be those of the constructor,
2520          * while the return type will be a reference to the constructor's class.
2521          * The constructor and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2522          * <p>
2523          * The requested type must have a return type of {@code void}.
2524          * (This is consistent with the JVM's treatment of constructor type descriptors.)
2525          * <p>
2526          * The returned method handle will have
2527          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2528          * the constructor's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2529          * <p>
2530          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the constructor's class will
2531          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2532          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2533          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2534 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2535 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2536 ...
2537 MethodHandle MH_newArrayList = publicLookup().findConstructor(
2538   ArrayList.class, methodType(void.class, Collection.class));
2539 Collection orig = Arrays.asList("x", "y");
2540 Collection copy = (ArrayList) MH_newArrayList.invokeExact(orig);
2541 assert(orig != copy);
2542 assertEquals(orig, copy);
2543 // a variable-arity constructor:
2544 MethodHandle MH_newProcessBuilder = publicLookup().findConstructor(
2545   ProcessBuilder.class, methodType(void.class, String[].class));
2546 ProcessBuilder pb = (ProcessBuilder)
2547   MH_newProcessBuilder.invoke("x", "y", "z");
2548 assertEquals("[x, y, z]", pb.command().toString());
2549          * }</pre></blockquote>
2550          *
2551          * @apiNote
2552          * This method does not find a static {@code <init>} factory method as it is invoked
2553          * via {@code invokestatic} bytecode as opposed to {@code invokespecial} for an
2554          * object constructor.  To look up static {@code <init>} factory method, use
2555          * the {@link #findStatic(Class, String, MethodType) findStatic} method.
2556          *
2557          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2558          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted, and a void return type
2559          * @return the desired method handle
2560          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the constructor does not exist
2561          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
2562          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2563          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2564          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2565          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2566          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2567          */
2568         public MethodHandle findConstructor(Class<?> refc, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2569             if (refc.isArray()) {
2570                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("no constructor for array class: " + refc.getName());
2571             }
2572             if (type.returnType() != void.class) {
2573                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("Constructors must have void return type: " + refc.getName());
2574             }
2575             String name = "<init>";
2576             MemberName ctor = resolveOrFail(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
2577             return getDirectConstructor(refc, ctor);
2578         }
2579 
2580         /**
2581          * Looks up a class by name from the lookup context defined by this {@code Lookup} object,
2582          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if resolved</a> by an {@code ldc} instruction.
2583          * Such a resolution, as specified in JVMS 5.4.3.1 section, attempts to locate and load the class,
2584          * and then determines whether the class is accessible to this lookup object.
2585          * <p>
2586          * The lookup context here is determined by the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class},
2587          * its class loader, and the {@linkplain #lookupModes() lookup modes}.
2588          *
2589          * @param targetName the fully qualified name of the class to be looked up.
2590          * @return the requested class.
2591          * @throws SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2592          *                           <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2593          * @throws LinkageError if the linkage fails
2594          * @throws ClassNotFoundException if the class cannot be loaded by the lookup class' loader.
2595          * @throws IllegalAccessException if the class is not accessible, using the allowed access
2596          * modes.
2597          * @since 9
2598          * @jvms 5.4.3.1 Class and Interface Resolution
2599          */
2600         public Class<?> findClass(String targetName) throws ClassNotFoundException, IllegalAccessException {
2601             Class<?> targetClass = Class.forName(targetName, false, lookupClass.getClassLoader());
2602             return accessClass(targetClass);
2603         }
2604 
2605         /**
2606          * Ensures that {@code targetClass} has been initialized. The class
2607          * to be initialized must be {@linkplain #accessClass accessible}
2608          * to this {@code Lookup} object.  This method causes {@code targetClass}
2609          * to be initialized if it has not been already initialized,
2610          * as specified in JVMS {@jvms 5.5}.
2611          *
2612          * @param targetClass the class to be initialized
2613          * @return {@code targetClass} that has been initialized
2614          *
2615          * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if {@code targetClass} is a primitive type or {@code void}
2616          *          or array class
2617          * @throws  IllegalAccessException if {@code targetClass} is not
2618          *          {@linkplain #accessClass accessible} to this lookup
2619          * @throws  ExceptionInInitializerError if the class initialization provoked
2620          *          by this method fails
2621          * @throws  SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2622          *          <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2623          * @since 15
2624          * @jvms 5.5 Initialization
2625          */
2626         public Class<?> ensureInitialized(Class<?> targetClass) throws IllegalAccessException {
2627             if (targetClass.isPrimitive())
2628                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(targetClass + " is a primitive class");
2629             if (targetClass.isArray())
2630                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(targetClass + " is an array class");
2631 
2632             if (!VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(targetClass, lookupClass, prevLookupClass, allowedModes)) {
2633                 throw new MemberName(targetClass).makeAccessException("access violation", this);
2634             }
2635             checkSecurityManager(targetClass, null);
2636 
2637             // ensure class initialization
2638             Unsafe.getUnsafe().ensureClassInitialized(targetClass);
2639             return targetClass;
2640         }
2641 
2642         /**
2643          * Determines if a class can be accessed from the lookup context defined by
2644          * this {@code Lookup} object. The static initializer of the class is not run.
2645          * <p>
2646          * If the {@code targetClass} is in the same module as the lookup class,
2647          * the lookup class is {@code LC} in module {@code M1} and
2648          * the previous lookup class is in module {@code M0} or
2649          * {@code null} if not present,
2650          * {@code targetClass} is accessible if and only if one of the following is true:
2651          * <ul>
2652          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PRIVATE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2653          *     {@code LC} or other class in the same nest of {@code LC}.</li>
2654          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PACKAGE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2655          *     in the same runtime package of {@code LC}.</li>
2656          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #MODULE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2657          *     a public type in {@code M1}.</li>
2658          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PUBLIC} access, {@code targetClass} is
2659          *     a public type in a package exported by {@code M1} to at least  {@code M0}
2660          *     if the previous lookup class is present; otherwise, {@code targetClass}
2661          *     is a public type in a package exported by {@code M1} unconditionally.</li>
2662          * </ul>
2663          *
2664          * <p>
2665          * Otherwise, if this lookup has {@link #UNCONDITIONAL} access, this lookup
2666          * can access public types in all modules when the type is in a package
2667          * that is exported unconditionally.
2668          * <p>
2669          * Otherwise, the target class is in a different module from {@code lookupClass},
2670          * and if this lookup does not have {@code PUBLIC} access, {@code lookupClass}
2671          * is inaccessible.
2672          * <p>
2673          * Otherwise, if this lookup has no {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class},
2674          * {@code M1} is the module containing {@code lookupClass} and
2675          * {@code M2} is the module containing {@code targetClass},
2676          * then {@code targetClass} is accessible if and only if
2677          * <ul>
2678          * <li>{@code M1} reads {@code M2}, and
2679          * <li>{@code targetClass} is public and in a package exported by
2680          *     {@code M2} at least to {@code M1}.
2681          * </ul>
2682          * <p>
2683          * Otherwise, if this lookup has a {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class},
2684          * {@code M1} and {@code M2} are as before, and {@code M0} is the module
2685          * containing the previous lookup class, then {@code targetClass} is accessible
2686          * if and only if one of the following is true:
2687          * <ul>
2688          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in {@code M0} and {@code M1}
2689          *     {@linkplain Module#reads reads} {@code M0} and the type is
2690          *     in a package that is exported to at least {@code M1}.
2691          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in {@code M1} and {@code M0}
2692          *     {@linkplain Module#reads reads} {@code M1} and the type is
2693          *     in a package that is exported to at least {@code M0}.
2694          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in a third module {@code M2} and both {@code M0}
2695          *     and {@code M1} reads {@code M2} and the type is in a package
2696          *     that is exported to at least both {@code M0} and {@code M2}.
2697          * </ul>
2698          * <p>
2699          * Otherwise, {@code targetClass} is not accessible.
2700          *
2701          * @param targetClass the class to be access-checked
2702          * @return the class that has been access-checked
2703          * @throws IllegalAccessException if the class is not accessible from the lookup class
2704          * and previous lookup class, if present, using the allowed access modes.
2705          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2706          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2707          * @since 9
2708          * @see <a href="#cross-module-lookup">Cross-module lookups</a>
2709          */
2710         public Class<?> accessClass(Class<?> targetClass) throws IllegalAccessException {
2711             if (!VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(targetClass, lookupClass, prevLookupClass, allowedModes)) {
2712                 throw new MemberName(targetClass).makeAccessException("access violation", this);
2713             }
2714             checkSecurityManager(targetClass, null);
2715             return targetClass;
2716         }
2717 
2718         /**
2719          * Produces an early-bound method handle for a virtual method.
2720          * It will bypass checks for overriding methods on the receiver,
2721          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if called</a> from an {@code invokespecial}
2722          * instruction from within the explicitly specified {@code specialCaller}.
2723          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2724          * with a suitably restricted receiver type prepended.
2725          * (The receiver type will be {@code specialCaller} or a subtype.)
2726          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible
2727          * to the lookup object.
2728          * <p>
2729          * Before method resolution,
2730          * if the explicitly specified caller class is not identical with the
2731          * lookup class, or if this lookup object does not have
2732          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private access</a>
2733          * privileges, the access fails.
2734          * <p>
2735          * The returned method handle will have
2736          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2737          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2738          * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
2739          * <em>(Note:  JVM internal methods named {@code "<init>"} are not visible to this API,
2740          * even though the {@code invokespecial} instruction can refer to them
2741          * in special circumstances.  Use {@link #findConstructor findConstructor}
2742          * to access instance initialization methods in a safe manner.)</em>
2743          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2744          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2745 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2746 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2747 ...
2748 static class Listie extends ArrayList {
2749   public String toString() { return "[wee Listie]"; }
2750   static Lookup lookup() { return MethodHandles.lookup(); }
2751 }
2752 ...
2753 // no access to constructor via invokeSpecial:
2754 MethodHandle MH_newListie = Listie.lookup()
2755   .findConstructor(Listie.class, methodType(void.class));
2756 Listie l = (Listie) MH_newListie.invokeExact();
2757 try { assertEquals("impossible", Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2758         Listie.class, "<init>", methodType(void.class), Listie.class));
2759  } catch (NoSuchMethodException ex) { } // OK
2760 // access to super and self methods via invokeSpecial:
2761 MethodHandle MH_super = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2762   ArrayList.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2763 MethodHandle MH_this = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2764   Listie.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2765 MethodHandle MH_duper = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2766   Object.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2767 assertEquals("[]", (String) MH_super.invokeExact(l));
2768 assertEquals(""+l, (String) MH_this.invokeExact(l));
2769 assertEquals("[]", (String) MH_duper.invokeExact(l)); // ArrayList method
2770 try { assertEquals("inaccessible", Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2771         String.class, "toString", methodType(String.class), Listie.class));
2772  } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) { } // OK
2773 Listie subl = new Listie() { public String toString() { return "[subclass]"; } };
2774 assertEquals(""+l, (String) MH_this.invokeExact(subl)); // Listie method
2775          * }</pre></blockquote>
2776          *
2777          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2778          * @param name the name of the method (which must not be "&lt;init&gt;")
2779          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
2780          * @param specialCaller the proposed calling class to perform the {@code invokespecial}
2781          * @return the desired method handle
2782          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2783          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2784          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
2785          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2786          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2787          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2788          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2789          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2790          */
2791         public MethodHandle findSpecial(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type,
2792                                         Class<?> specialCaller) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2793             checkSpecialCaller(specialCaller, refc);
2794             Lookup specialLookup = this.in(specialCaller);
2795             MemberName method = specialLookup.resolveOrFail(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
2796             return specialLookup.getDirectMethod(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2797         }
2798 
2799         /**
2800          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a non-static field.
2801          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
2802          * value type.
2803          * The method handle's single argument will be the instance containing
2804          * the field.
2805          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2806          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2807          * @param name the field's name
2808          * @param type the field's type
2809          * @return a method handle which can load values from the field
2810          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2811          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2812          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2813          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2814          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2815          * @see #findVarHandle(Class, String, Class)
2816          */
2817         public MethodHandle findGetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2818             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_getField, refc, name, type);
2819             return getDirectField(REF_getField, refc, field);
2820         }
2821 
2822         /**
2823          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a non-static field.
2824          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
2825          * The method handle will take two arguments, the instance containing
2826          * the field, and the value to be stored.
2827          * The second argument will be of the field's value type.
2828          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2829          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2830          * @param name the field's name
2831          * @param type the field's type
2832          * @return a method handle which can store values into the field
2833          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2834          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2835          *                                or {@code final}
2836          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2837          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2838          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2839          * @see #findVarHandle(Class, String, Class)
2840          */
2841         public MethodHandle findSetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2842             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_putField, refc, name, type);
2843             return getDirectField(REF_putField, refc, field);
2844         }

2846         /**
2847          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a non-static field {@code name}
2848          * of type {@code type} declared in a class of type {@code recv}.
2849          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code type} and it has one
2850          * coordinate type, {@code recv}.
2851          * <p>
2852          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
2853          * class.
2854          * <p>
2855          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
2856          * the following conditions:
2857          * <ul>
2858          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
2859          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
2860          *     modes are unsupported.
2861          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
2862          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
2863          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
2864          *     access modes are unsupported.
2865          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
2866          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
2867          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
2868          *     unsupported.
2869          * </ul>
2870          * <p>
2871          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
2872          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
2873          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
2874          * access modes.
2875          * <p>
2876          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
2877          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
2878          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
2879          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
2880          * @apiNote
2881          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
2882          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
2883          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
2884          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
2885          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
2886          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
2887          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
2888          * unexpectedly fail.
2889          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
2890          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
2891          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
2892          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
2893          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
2894          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
2895          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
2896          * details).
2897          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
2898          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
2899          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
2900          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
2901          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
2902          * @param recv the receiver class, of type {@code R}, that declares the
2903          * non-static field
2904          * @param name the field's name
2905          * @param type the field's type, of type {@code T}
2906          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields.
2907          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2908          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2909          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2910          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2911          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2912          * @since 9
2913          */
2914         public VarHandle findVarHandle(Class<?> recv, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2915             MemberName getField = resolveOrFail(REF_getField, recv, name, type);
2916             MemberName putField = resolveOrFail(REF_putField, recv, name, type);
2917             return getFieldVarHandle(REF_getField, REF_putField, recv, getField, putField);
2918         }
2919 
2920         /**
2921          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a static field.
2922          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
2923          * value type.
2924          * The method handle will take no arguments.
2925          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2926          * <p>
2927          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
2928          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2929          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2930          * @param name the field's name
2931          * @param type the field's type
2932          * @return a method handle which can load values from the field
2933          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2934          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2935          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2936          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2937          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2938          */
2939         public MethodHandle findStaticGetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2940             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_getStatic, refc, name, type);
2941             return getDirectField(REF_getStatic, refc, field);
2942         }

2944         /**
2945          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a static field.
2946          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
2947          * The method handle will take a single
2948          * argument, of the field's value type, the value to be stored.
2949          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2950          * <p>
2951          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
2952          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2953          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2954          * @param name the field's name
2955          * @param type the field's type
2956          * @return a method handle which can store values into the field
2957          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2958          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2959          *                                or is {@code final}
2960          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2961          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2962          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2963          */
2964         public MethodHandle findStaticSetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2965             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_putStatic, refc, name, type);
2966             return getDirectField(REF_putStatic, refc, field);
2967         }
2968 
2969         /**
2970          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a static field {@code name} of
2971          * type {@code type} declared in a class of type {@code decl}.
2972          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code type} and it has no
2973          * coordinate types.
2974          * <p>
2975          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
2976          * class.
2977          * <p>
2978          * If the returned VarHandle is operated on, the declaring class will be
2979          * initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2980          * <p>
2981          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
2982          * the following conditions:
2983          * <ul>
2984          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
2985          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
2986          *     modes are unsupported.
2987          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
2988          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
2989          *     {@code float}, or {@code double}, then numeric atomic update
2990          *     access modes are unsupported.
2991          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
2992          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
2993          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
2994          *     unsupported.
2995          * </ul>
2996          * <p>
2997          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
2998          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
2999          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
3000          * access modes.
3001          * <p>
3002          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3003          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3004          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3005          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3006          * @apiNote
3007          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3008          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3009          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3010          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3011          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3012          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3013          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3014          * unexpectedly fail.
3015          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3016          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3017          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3018          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3019          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3020          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3021          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3022          * details).
3023          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3024          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
3025          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
3026          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
3027          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
3028          * @param decl the class that declares the static field
3029          * @param name the field's name
3030          * @param type the field's type, of type {@code T}
3031          * @return a VarHandle giving access to a static field
3032          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
3033          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
3034          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3035          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3036          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3037          * @since 9
3038          */
3039         public VarHandle findStaticVarHandle(Class<?> decl, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
3040             MemberName getField = resolveOrFail(REF_getStatic, decl, name, type);
3041             MemberName putField = resolveOrFail(REF_putStatic, decl, name, type);
3042             return getFieldVarHandle(REF_getStatic, REF_putStatic, decl, getField, putField);
3043         }
3044 
3045         /**
3046          * Produces an early-bound method handle for a non-static method.
3047          * The receiver must have a supertype {@code defc} in which a method
3048          * of the given name and type is accessible to the lookup class.
3049          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
3050          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3051          * without any insertion of an additional receiver parameter.
3052          * The given receiver will be bound into the method handle,
3053          * so that every call to the method handle will invoke the
3054          * requested method on the given receiver.
3055          * <p>
3056          * The returned method handle will have
3057          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3058          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set
3059          * <em>and</em> the trailing array argument is not the only argument.
3060          * (If the trailing array argument is the only argument,
3061          * the given receiver value will be bound to it.)
3062          * <p>
3063          * This is almost equivalent to the following code, with some differences noted below:
3064          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
3065 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
3066 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
3067 ...
3068 MethodHandle mh0 = lookup().findVirtual(defc, name, type);
3069 MethodHandle mh1 = mh0.bindTo(receiver);
3070 mh1 = mh1.withVarargs(mh0.isVarargsCollector());
3071 return mh1;
3072          * }</pre></blockquote>
3073          * where {@code defc} is either {@code receiver.getClass()} or a super
3074          * type of that class, in which the requested method is accessible
3075          * to the lookup class.
3076          * (Unlike {@code bind}, {@code bindTo} does not preserve variable arity.
3077          * Also, {@code bindTo} may throw a {@code ClassCastException} in instances where {@code bind} would
3078          * throw an {@code IllegalAccessException}, as in the case where the member is {@code protected} and
3079          * the receiver is restricted by {@code findVirtual} to the lookup class.)
3080          * @param receiver the object from which the method is accessed
3081          * @param name the name of the method
3082          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
3083          * @return the desired method handle
3084          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
3085          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3086          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3087          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3088          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3089          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3090          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3091          * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
3092          * @see #findVirtual
3093          */
3094         public MethodHandle bind(Object receiver, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
3095             Class<? extends Object> refc = receiver.getClass(); // may get NPE
3096             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
3097             MethodHandle mh = getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3098             if (!mh.type().leadingReferenceParameter().isAssignableFrom(receiver.getClass())) {
3099                 throw new IllegalAccessException("The restricted defining class " +
3100                                                  mh.type().leadingReferenceParameter().getName() +
3101                                                  " is not assignable from receiver class " +
3102                                                  receiver.getClass().getName());
3103             }
3104             return mh.bindArgumentL(0, receiver).setVarargs(method);
3105         }
3106 
3107         /**
3108          * Makes a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3109          * to <i>m</i>, if the lookup class has permission.
3110          * If <i>m</i> is non-static, the receiver argument is treated as an initial argument.
3111          * If <i>m</i> is virtual, overriding is respected on every call.
3112          * Unlike the Core Reflection API, exceptions are <em>not</em> wrapped.
3113          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3114          * with the receiver type prepended (but only if it is non-static).
3115          * If the method's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3116          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3117          * If <i>m</i> is not public, do not share the resulting handle with untrusted parties.
3118          * <p>
3119          * The returned method handle will have
3120          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3121          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3122          * <p>
3123          * If <i>m</i> is static, and
3124          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the method's class will
3125          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3126          * @param m the reflected method
3127          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected method
3128          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3129          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3130          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3131          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3132          */
3133         public MethodHandle unreflect(Method m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3134             if (m.getDeclaringClass() == MethodHandle.class) {
3135                 MethodHandle mh = unreflectForMH(m);
3136                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
3137             }
3138             if (m.getDeclaringClass() == VarHandle.class) {
3139                 MethodHandle mh = unreflectForVH(m);
3140                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
3141             }
3142             MemberName method = new MemberName(m);
3143             byte refKind = method.getReferenceKind();
3144             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial)
3145                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3146             assert(method.isMethod());
3147             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3148             Lookup lookup = m.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3149             return lookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, method.getDeclaringClass(), method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3150         }
3151         private MethodHandle unreflectForMH(Method m) {
3152             // these names require special lookups because they throw UnsupportedOperationException
3153             if (MemberName.isMethodHandleInvokeName(m.getName()))
3154                 return MethodHandleImpl.fakeMethodHandleInvoke(new MemberName(m));
3155             return null;
3156         }
3157         private MethodHandle unreflectForVH(Method m) {
3158             // these names require special lookups because they throw UnsupportedOperationException
3159             if (MemberName.isVarHandleMethodInvokeName(m.getName()))
3160                 return MethodHandleImpl.fakeVarHandleInvoke(new MemberName(m));
3161             return null;
3162         }

3164         /**
3165          * Produces a method handle for a reflected method.
3166          * It will bypass checks for overriding methods on the receiver,
3167          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if called</a> from an {@code invokespecial}
3168          * instruction from within the explicitly specified {@code specialCaller}.
3169          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3170          * with a suitably restricted receiver type prepended.
3171          * (The receiver type will be {@code specialCaller} or a subtype.)
3172          * If the method's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3173          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class,
3174          * as if {@code invokespecial} instruction were being linked.
3175          * <p>
3176          * Before method resolution,
3177          * if the explicitly specified caller class is not identical with the
3178          * lookup class, or if this lookup object does not have
3179          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private access</a>
3180          * privileges, the access fails.
3181          * <p>
3182          * The returned method handle will have
3183          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3184          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3185          * @param m the reflected method
3186          * @param specialCaller the class nominally calling the method
3187          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected method
3188          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
3189          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
3190          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3191          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3192          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3193          */
3194         public MethodHandle unreflectSpecial(Method m, Class<?> specialCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3195             checkSpecialCaller(specialCaller, m.getDeclaringClass());
3196             Lookup specialLookup = this.in(specialCaller);
3197             MemberName method = new MemberName(m, true);
3198             assert(method.isMethod());
3199             // ignore m.isAccessible:  this is a new kind of access
3200             return specialLookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(REF_invokeSpecial, method.getDeclaringClass(), method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3201         }
3202 
3203         /**
3204          * Produces a method handle for a reflected constructor.
3205          * The type of the method handle will be that of the constructor,
3206          * with the return type changed to the declaring class.
3207          * The method handle will perform a {@code newInstance} operation,
3208          * creating a new instance of the constructor's class on the
3209          * arguments passed to the method handle.
3210          * <p>
3211          * If the constructor's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3212          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3213          * <p>
3214          * The returned method handle will have
3215          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3216          * the constructor's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3217          * <p>
3218          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the constructor's class will
3219          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3220          * @param c the reflected constructor
3221          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected constructor
3222          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3223          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3224          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3225          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3226          */
3227         public MethodHandle unreflectConstructor(Constructor<?> c) throws IllegalAccessException {
3228             MemberName ctor = new MemberName(c);
3229             assert(ctor.isObjectConstructorOrStaticInitMethod());
3230             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3231             Lookup lookup = c.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3232             if (ctor.isObjectConstructor()) {
3233                 assert(ctor.getReturnType() == void.class);
3234                 return lookup.getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(ctor.getDeclaringClass(), ctor);
3235             } else {
3236                 // static init factory is a static method
3237                 assert(ctor.isMethod() && ctor.getReturnType() == ctor.getDeclaringClass() && ctor.getReferenceKind() == REF_invokeStatic);
3238                 assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // must not be caller-sensitive
3239                 return lookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(ctor.getReferenceKind(), ctor.getDeclaringClass(), ctor, lookup);
3240             }
3241         }

3243         /**
3244          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a reflected field.
3245          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
3246          * value type.
3247          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take no arguments.
3248          * Otherwise, its single argument will be the instance containing
3249          * the field.
3250          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3251          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3252          * <p>
3253          * If the field is static, and
3254          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3255          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3256          * @param f the reflected field
3257          * @return a method handle which can load values from the reflected field
3258          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3259          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3260          */
3261         public MethodHandle unreflectGetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3262             return unreflectField(f, false);
3263         }
3264 
3265         /**
3266          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a reflected field.
3267          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3268          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take a single
3269          * argument, of the field's value type, the value to be stored.
3270          * Otherwise, the two arguments will be the instance containing
3271          * the field, and the value to be stored.
3272          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3273          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3274          * <p>
3275          * If the field is {@code final}, write access will not be
3276          * allowed and access checking will fail, except under certain
3277          * narrow circumstances documented for {@link Field#set Field.set}.
3278          * A method handle is returned only if a corresponding call to
3279          * the {@code Field} object's {@code set} method could return
3280          * normally.  In particular, fields which are both {@code static}
3281          * and {@code final} may never be set.
3282          * <p>
3283          * If the field is {@code static}, and
3284          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3285          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3286          * @param f the reflected field
3287          * @return a method handle which can store values into the reflected field
3288          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
3289          *         or if the field is {@code final} and write access
3290          *         is not enabled on the {@code Field} object
3291          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3292          */
3293         public MethodHandle unreflectSetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3294             return unreflectField(f, true);
3295         }
3296 
3297         private MethodHandle unreflectField(Field f, boolean isSetter) throws IllegalAccessException {
3298             MemberName field = new MemberName(f, isSetter);
3299             if (isSetter && field.isFinal()) {
3300                 if (field.isTrustedFinalField()) {
3301                     String msg = field.isStatic() ? "static final field has no write access"
3302                                                   : "final field has no write access";
3303                     throw field.makeAccessException(msg, this);
3304                 }
3305             }
3306             assert(isSetter
3307                     ? MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(field.getReferenceKind())
3308                     : MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(field.getReferenceKind()));
3309             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3310             Lookup lookup = f.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3311             return lookup.getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(field.getReferenceKind(), f.getDeclaringClass(), field);
3312         }
