3314         /**
3315          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a reflected field {@code f}
3316          * of type {@code T} declared in a class of type {@code R}.
3317          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code T}.
3318          * If the field is non-static the VarHandle has one coordinate type,
3319          * {@code R}.  Otherwise, the field is static, and the VarHandle has no
3320          * coordinate types.
3321          * <p>
3322          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
3323          * class, regardless of the value of the field's {@code accessible}
3324          * flag.
3325          * <p>
3326          * If the field is static, and if the returned VarHandle is operated
3327          * on, the field's declaring class will be initialized, if it has not
3328          * already been initialized.
3329          * <p>
3330          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3331          * the following conditions:
3332          * <ul>
3333          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
3334          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
3335          *     modes are unsupported.
3336          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
3337          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3338          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
3339          *     access modes are unsupported.
3340          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3341          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3342          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3343          *     unsupported.
3344          * </ul>
3345          * <p>
3346          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
3347          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
3348          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
3349          * access modes.
3350          * <p>
3351          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3352          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3353          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3354          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3355          * @apiNote
3356          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3357          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3358          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3359          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3360          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3361          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3362          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3363          * unexpectedly fail.
3364          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3365          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3366          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3367          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3368          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3369          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3370          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3371          * details).
3372          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3373          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
3374          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
3375          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
3376          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
3377          * @param f the reflected field, with a field of type {@code T}, and
3378          * a declaring class of type {@code R}
3379          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields or a static
3380          * field
3381          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3382          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3383          * @since 9
3384          */
3385         public VarHandle unreflectVarHandle(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3386             MemberName getField = new MemberName(f, false);
3387             MemberName putField = new MemberName(f, true);
3388             return getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(getField.getReferenceKind(), putField.getReferenceKind(),
3389                                                       f.getDeclaringClass(), getField, putField);
3390         }
3391 
3392         /**
3393          * Cracks a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3394          * created by this lookup object or a similar one.
3395          * Security and access checks are performed to ensure that this lookup object
3396          * is capable of reproducing the target method handle.
3397          * This means that the cracking may fail if target is a direct method handle
3398          * but was created by an unrelated lookup object.
3399          * This can happen if the method handle is <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#callsens">caller sensitive</a>
3400          * and was created by a lookup object for a different class.
3401          * @param target a direct method handle to crack into symbolic reference components
3402          * @return a symbolic reference which can be used to reconstruct this method handle from this lookup object
3403          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3404          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3405          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the target is not a direct method handle or if access checking fails
3406          * @throws    NullPointerException if the target is {@code null}
3407          * @see MethodHandleInfo
3408          * @since 1.8
3409          */
3410         public MethodHandleInfo revealDirect(MethodHandle target) {
3411             if (!target.isCrackable()) {
3412                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("not a direct method handle");
3413             }
3414             MemberName member = target.internalMemberName();
3415             Class<?> defc = member.getDeclaringClass();
3416             byte refKind = member.getReferenceKind();
3417             assert(MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind));
3418             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial && !target.isInvokeSpecial())
3419                 // Devirtualized method invocation is usually formally virtual.
3420                 // To avoid creating extra MemberName objects for this common case,
3421                 // we encode this extra degree of freedom using MH.isInvokeSpecial.
3422                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3423             if (refKind == REF_invokeVirtual && defc.isInterface())
3424                 // Symbolic reference is through interface but resolves to Object method (toString, etc.)
3425                 refKind = REF_invokeInterface;
3426             // Check SM permissions and member access before cracking.
3427             try {
3428                 checkAccess(refKind, defc, member);
3429                 checkSecurityManager(defc, member);
3430             } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) {
3431                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
3432             }
3433             if (allowedModes != TRUSTED && member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3434                 Class<?> callerClass = target.internalCallerClass();
3435                 if (!hasFullPrivilegeAccess() || callerClass != lookupClass())
3436                     throw new IllegalArgumentException("method handle is caller sensitive: "+callerClass);
3437             }
3438             // Produce the handle to the results.
3439             return new InfoFromMemberName(this, member, refKind);
3440         }
3441 
3442         /// Helper methods, all package-private.
3443 
3444         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
3445             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3446             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3447             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3448             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3449                                             NoSuchFieldException.class);
3450         }
3451 
3452         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
3453             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3454             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3455             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3456             checkMethodName(refKind, name);  // NPE check on name
3457             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3458                                             NoSuchMethodException.class);
3459         }
3460 
3461         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, MemberName member) throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3462             checkSymbolicClass(member.getDeclaringClass());  // do this before attempting to resolve
3463             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3464             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3465             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull(),
3466                                             ReflectiveOperationException.class);
3467         }
3468 
3469         MemberName resolveOrNull(byte refKind, MemberName member) {
3470             // do this before attempting to resolve
3471             if (!isClassAccessible(member.getDeclaringClass())) {
3472                 return null;
3473             }
3474             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3475             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3476             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull());
3477         }
3478 
3479         void checkSymbolicClass(Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3480             if (!isClassAccessible(refc)) {
3481                 throw new MemberName(refc).makeAccessException("symbolic reference class is not accessible", this);
3482             }
3483         }
3484 
3485         boolean isClassAccessible(Class<?> refc) {
3486             Objects.requireNonNull(refc);
3487             Class<?> caller = lookupClassOrNull();
3488             return caller == null || VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, caller, prevLookupClass, allowedModes);
3489         }
3490 
3491         /** Check name for an illegal leading "&lt;" character. */
3492         void checkMethodName(byte refKind, String name) throws NoSuchMethodException {
3493             // "<init>" can only be invoked via invokespecial or it's a static init factory
3494             if (name.startsWith("<") && refKind != REF_newInvokeSpecial &&
3495                     !(refKind == REF_invokeStatic && name.equals("<init>"))) {
3496                     throw new NoSuchMethodException("illegal method name: " + name);
3497             }
3498         }
3499 
3500         /**
3501          * Find my trustable caller class if m is a caller sensitive method.
3502          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3503          * Otherwise, if m is caller-sensitive, throw IllegalAccessException.
3504          */
3505         Lookup findBoundCallerLookup(MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3506             if (MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(m) && !hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
3507                 // Only lookups with full privilege access are allowed to resolve caller-sensitive methods
3508                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3509             }
3510             return this;
3511         }
3512 
3513         /**
3514          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3515          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3516          *
3517          * @deprecated This method was originally designed to test {@code PRIVATE} access
3518          * that implies full privilege access but {@code MODULE} access has since become
3519          * independent of {@code PRIVATE} access.  It is recommended to call
3520          * {@link #hasFullPrivilegeAccess()} instead.
3521          * @since 9
3522          */
3523         @Deprecated(since="14")
3524         public boolean hasPrivateAccess() {
3525             return hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3526         }
3527 
3528         /**
3529          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has <em>full privilege access</em>,
3530          * i.e. {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3531          * A {@code Lookup} object must have full privilege access in order to
3532          * access all members that are allowed to the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class}.
3533          *
3534          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has full privilege access.
3535          * @since 14
3536          * @see <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private and module access</a>
3537          */
3538         public boolean hasFullPrivilegeAccess() {
3539             return (allowedModes & (PRIVATE|MODULE)) == (PRIVATE|MODULE);
3540         }
3541 
3542         /**
3543          * Perform necessary <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">access checks</a>.
3544          * Determines a trustable caller class to compare with refc, the symbolic reference class.
3545          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3546          */
3547         void checkSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3548             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3549 
3550             SecurityManager smgr = System.getSecurityManager();
3551             if (smgr == null)  return;
3552 
3553             // Step 1:
3554             boolean fullPowerLookup = hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3555             if (!fullPowerLookup ||
3556                 !VerifyAccess.classLoaderIsAncestor(lookupClass, refc)) {
3557                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(refc);
3558             }
3559 
3560             if (m == null) {  // findClass or accessClass
3561                 // Step 2b:
3562                 if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3563                     smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.GET_CLASSLOADER_PERMISSION);
3564                 }
3565                 return;
3566             }
3567 
3568             // Step 2a:
3569             if (m.isPublic()) return;
3570             if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3571                 smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.CHECK_MEMBER_ACCESS_PERMISSION);
3572             }
3573 
3574             // Step 3:
3575             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3576             if (!fullPowerLookup && defc != refc) {
3577                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(defc);
3578             }
3579         }
3580 
3581         void checkMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3582             boolean wantStatic = (refKind == REF_invokeStatic);
3583             String message;
3584             if (m.isObjectConstructor())
3585                 message = "expected a method, not a constructor";
3586             else if (!m.isMethod())
3587                 message = "expected a method";
3588             else if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3589                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static method" : "expected a non-static method";
3590             else
3591                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3592             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3593         }
3594 
3595         void checkField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3596             boolean wantStatic = !MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind);
3597             String message;
3598             if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3599                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static field" : "expected a non-static field";
3600             else
3601                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3602             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3603         }
3604 
3605         /** Check public/protected/private bits on the symbolic reference class and its member. */
3606         void checkAccess(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3607             assert(m.referenceKindIsConsistentWith(refKind) &&
3608                    MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind) &&
3609                    (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind) == m.isField()));
3610             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3611             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3612             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3613             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) &&
3614                     refKind == REF_invokeVirtual &&
3615                     m.getDeclaringClass() == Object.class &&
3616                     m.getName().equals("clone") &&
3617                     refc.isArray()) {
3618                 // The JVM does this hack also.
3619                 // (See ClassVerifier::verify_invoke_instructions
3620                 // and LinkResolver::check_method_accessability.)
3621                 // Because the JVM does not allow separate methods on array types,
3622                 // there is no separate method for int[].clone.
3623                 // All arrays simply inherit Object.clone.
3624                 // But for access checking logic, we make Object.clone
3625                 // (normally protected) appear to be public.
3626                 // Later on, when the DirectMethodHandle is created,
3627                 // its leading argument will be restricted to the
3628                 // requested array type.
3629                 // N.B. The return type is not adjusted, because
3630                 // that is *not* the bytecode behavior.
3631                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED | Modifier.PUBLIC;
3632             }
3633             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) && refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3634                 // cannot "new" a protected ctor in a different package
3635                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED;
3636             }
3637             if (Modifier.isFinal(mods) &&
3638                     MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(refKind))
3639                 throw m.makeAccessException("unexpected set of a final field", this);
3640             int requestedModes = fixmods(mods);  // adjust 0 => PACKAGE
3641             if ((requestedModes & allowedModes) != 0) {
3642                 if (VerifyAccess.isMemberAccessible(refc, m.getDeclaringClass(),
3643                                                     mods, lookupClass(), previousLookupClass(), allowedModes))
3644                     return;
3645             } else {
3646                 // Protected members can also be checked as if they were package-private.
3647                 if ((requestedModes & PROTECTED) != 0 && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0
3648                         && VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(m.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3649                     return;
3650             }
3651             throw m.makeAccessException(accessFailedMessage(refc, m), this);
3652         }
3653 
3654         String accessFailedMessage(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3655             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3656             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3657             // check the class first:
3658             boolean classOK = (Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) &&
3659                                (defc == refc ||
3660                                 Modifier.isPublic(refc.getModifiers())));
3661             if (!classOK && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0) {
3662                 // ignore previous lookup class to check if default package access
3663                 classOK = (VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(defc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES) &&
3664                            (defc == refc ||
3665                             VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES)));
3666             }
3667             if (!classOK)
3668                 return "class is not public";
3669             if (Modifier.isPublic(mods))
3670                 return "access to public member failed";  // (how?, module not readable?)
3671             if (Modifier.isPrivate(mods))
3672                 return "member is private";
3673             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods))
3674                 return "member is protected";
3675             return "member is private to package";
3676         }
3677 
3678         private void checkSpecialCaller(Class<?> specialCaller, Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3679             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3680             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3681             if ((lookupModes() & PRIVATE) == 0
3682                 || (specialCaller != lookupClass()
3683                        // ensure non-abstract methods in superinterfaces can be special-invoked
3684                     && !(refc != null && refc.isInterface() && refc.isAssignableFrom(specialCaller))))
3685                 throw new MemberName(specialCaller).
3686                     makeAccessException("no private access for invokespecial", this);
3687         }
3688 
3689         private boolean restrictProtectedReceiver(MemberName method) {
3690             // The accessing class only has the right to use a protected member
3691             // on itself or a subclass.  Enforce that restriction, from JVMS 5.4.4, etc.
3692             if (!method.isProtected() || method.isStatic()
3693                 || allowedModes == TRUSTED
3694                 || method.getDeclaringClass() == lookupClass()
3695                 || VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(method.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3696                 return false;
3697             return true;
3698         }
3699         private MethodHandle restrictReceiver(MemberName method, DirectMethodHandle mh, Class<?> caller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3700             assert(!method.isStatic());
3701             // receiver type of mh is too wide; narrow to caller
3702             if (!method.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(caller)) {
3703                 throw method.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", caller);
3704             }
3705             MethodType rawType = mh.type();
3706             if (caller.isAssignableFrom(rawType.parameterType(0))) return mh; // no need to restrict; already narrow
3707             MethodType narrowType = rawType.changeParameterType(0, caller);
3708             assert(!mh.isVarargsCollector());  // viewAsType will lose varargs-ness
3709             assert(mh.viewAsTypeChecks(narrowType, true));
3710             return mh.copyWith(narrowType, mh.form);
3711         }
3712 
3713         /** Check access and get the requested method. */
3714         private MethodHandle getDirectMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3715             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3716             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3717             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3718         }
3719         /** Check access and get the requested method, for invokespecial with no restriction on the application of narrowing rules. */
3720         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3721             final boolean doRestrict    = false;
3722             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3723             return getDirectMethodCommon(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3724         }
3725         /** Check access and get the requested method, eliding security manager checks. */
3726         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3727             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3728             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3729             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3730         }
3731         /** Common code for all methods; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3732         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method,
3733                                                    boolean checkSecurity,
3734                                                    boolean doRestrict,
3735                                                    Lookup boundCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3736             checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3737             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3738             if (checkSecurity)
3739                 checkSecurityManager(refc, method);
3740             assert(!method.isMethodHandleInvoke());
3741 
3742             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial &&
3743                 refc != lookupClass() &&
3744                 !refc.isInterface() &&
3745                 refc != lookupClass().getSuperclass() &&
3746                 refc.isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3747                 assert(!method.getName().equals("<init>"));  // not this code path
3748 
3749                 // Per JVMS 6.5, desc. of invokespecial instruction:
3750                 // If the method is in a superclass of the LC,
3751                 // and if our original search was above LC.super,
3752                 // repeat the search (symbolic lookup) from LC.super
3753                 // and continue with the direct superclass of that class,
3754                 // and so forth, until a match is found or no further superclasses exist.
3755                 // FIXME: MemberName.resolve should handle this instead.
3756                 Class<?> refcAsSuper = lookupClass();
3757                 MemberName m2;
3758                 do {
3759                     refcAsSuper = refcAsSuper.getSuperclass();
3760                     m2 = new MemberName(refcAsSuper,
3761                                         method.getName(),
3762                                         method.getMethodType(),
3763                                         REF_invokeSpecial);
3764                     m2 = IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, m2, lookupClassOrNull());
3765                 } while (m2 == null &&         // no method is found yet
3766                          refc != refcAsSuper); // search up to refc
3767                 if (m2 == null)  throw new InternalError(method.toString());
3768                 method = m2;
3769                 refc = refcAsSuper;
3770                 // redo basic checks
3771                 checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3772             }
3773             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refKind, refc, method, lookupClass());
3774             MethodHandle mh = dmh;
3775             // Optionally narrow the receiver argument to lookupClass using restrictReceiver.
3776             if ((doRestrict && refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) ||
3777                     (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) && restrictProtectedReceiver(method))) {
3778                 mh = restrictReceiver(method, dmh, lookupClass());
3779             }
3780             mh = maybeBindCaller(method, mh, boundCaller);
3781             mh = mh.setVarargs(method);
3782             return mh;
3783         }
3784         private MethodHandle maybeBindCaller(MemberName method, MethodHandle mh, Lookup boundCaller)
3785                                              throws IllegalAccessException {
3786             if (boundCaller.allowedModes == TRUSTED || !MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(method))
3787                 return mh;
3788 
3789             // boundCaller must have full privilege access.
3790             // It should have been checked by findBoundCallerLookup. Safe to check this again.
3791             if (!boundCaller.hasFullPrivilegeAccess())
3792                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3793 
3794             MethodHandle cbmh = MethodHandleImpl.bindCaller(mh, boundCaller.lookupClass);
3795             // Note: caller will apply varargs after this step happens.
3796             return cbmh;
3797         }
3798 
3799         /** Check access and get the requested field. */
3800         private MethodHandle getDirectField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3801             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3802             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3803         }
3804         /** Check access and get the requested field, eliding security manager checks. */
3805         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3806             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3807             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3808         }
3809         /** Common code for all fields; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3810         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field,
3811                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3812             checkField(refKind, refc, field);
3813             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3814             if (checkSecurity)
3815                 checkSecurityManager(refc, field);
3816             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refc, field);
3817             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) &&
3818                                     restrictProtectedReceiver(field));
3819             if (doRestrict)
3820                 return restrictReceiver(field, dmh, lookupClass());
3821             return dmh;
3822         }
3823         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandle(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3824                                             Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3825                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3826             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3827             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3828         }
3829         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3830                                                              Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3831                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3832             final boolean checkSecurity = false;
3833             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3834         }
3835         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleCommon(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3836                                                   Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField,
3837                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3838             assert getField.isStatic() == putField.isStatic();
3839             assert getField.isGetter() && putField.isSetter();
3840             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(getRefKind) == MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(putRefKind);
3841             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(getRefKind) && MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(putRefKind);
3842 
3843             checkField(getRefKind, refc, getField);
3844             if (checkSecurity)
3845                 checkSecurityManager(refc, getField);
3846 
3847             if (!putField.isFinal()) {
3848                 // A VarHandle does not support updates to final fields, any
3849                 // such VarHandle to a final field will be read-only and
3850                 // therefore the following write-based accessibility checks are
3851                 // only required for non-final fields
3852                 checkField(putRefKind, refc, putField);
3853                 if (checkSecurity)
3854                     checkSecurityManager(refc, putField);
3855             }
3856 
3857             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(getRefKind) &&
3858                                   restrictProtectedReceiver(getField));
3859             if (doRestrict) {
3860                 assert !getField.isStatic();
3861                 // receiver type of VarHandle is too wide; narrow to caller
3862                 if (!getField.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3863                     throw getField.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", lookupClass());
3864                 }
3865                 refc = lookupClass();
3866             }
3867             return VarHandles.makeFieldHandle(getField, refc, getField.getFieldType(),
3868                                               this.allowedModes == TRUSTED && !getField.isTrustedFinalField());
3869         }
3870         /** Check access and get the requested constructor. */
3871         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructor(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3872             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3873             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3874         }
3875         /** Check access and get the requested constructor, eliding security manager checks. */
3876         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3877             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3878             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3879         }
3880         /** Common code for all constructors; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3881         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorCommon(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor,
3882                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3883             assert(ctor.isObjectConstructor());
3884             checkAccess(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, ctor);
3885             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3886             if (checkSecurity)
3887                 checkSecurityManager(refc, ctor);
3888             assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // maybeBindCaller not relevant here
3889             return DirectMethodHandle.make(ctor).setVarargs(ctor);
3890         }
3891 
3892         /** Hook called from the JVM (via MethodHandleNatives) to link MH constants:
3893          */
3894         /*non-public*/
3895         MethodHandle linkMethodHandleConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, String name, Object type)
3896                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3897             if (!(type instanceof Class || type instanceof MethodType))
3898                 throw new InternalError("unresolved MemberName");
3899             MemberName member = new MemberName(refKind, defc, name, type);
3900             MethodHandle mh = LOOKASIDE_TABLE.get(member);
3901             if (mh != null) {
3902                 checkSymbolicClass(defc);
3903                 return mh;
3904             }
3905             if (defc == MethodHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3906                 // Treat MethodHandle.invoke and invokeExact specially.
3907                 mh = findVirtualForMH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3908                 if (mh != null) {
3909                     return mh;
3910                 }
3911             } else if (defc == VarHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3912                 // Treat signature-polymorphic methods on VarHandle specially.
3913                 mh = findVirtualForVH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3914                 if (mh != null) {
3915                     return mh;
3916                 }
3917             }
3918             MemberName resolved = resolveOrFail(refKind, member);
3919             mh = getDirectMethodForConstant(refKind, defc, resolved);
3920             if (mh instanceof DirectMethodHandle
3921                     && canBeCached(refKind, defc, resolved)) {
3922                 MemberName key = mh.internalMemberName();
3923                 if (key != null) {
3924                     key = key.asNormalOriginal();
3925                 }
3926                 if (member.equals(key)) {  // better safe than sorry
3927                     LOOKASIDE_TABLE.put(key, (DirectMethodHandle) mh);
3928                 }
3929             }
3930             return mh;
3931         }
3932         private boolean canBeCached(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member) {
3933             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) {
3934                 return false;
3935             }
3936             if (!Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) ||
3937                     !Modifier.isPublic(member.getDeclaringClass().getModifiers()) ||
3938                     !member.isPublic() ||
3939                     member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3940                 return false;
3941             }
3942             ClassLoader loader = defc.getClassLoader();
3943             if (loader != null) {
3944                 ClassLoader sysl = ClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader();
3945                 boolean found = false;
3946                 while (sysl != null) {
3947                     if (loader == sysl) { found = true; break; }
3948                     sysl = sysl.getParent();
3949                 }
3950                 if (!found) {
3951                     return false;
3952                 }
3953             }
3954             try {
3955                 MemberName resolved2 = publicLookup().resolveOrNull(refKind,
3956                     new MemberName(refKind, defc, member.getName(), member.getType()));
3957                 if (resolved2 == null) {
3958                     return false;
3959                 }
3960                 checkSecurityManager(defc, resolved2);
3961             } catch (SecurityException ex) {
3962                 return false;
3963             }
3964             return true;
3965         }
3966         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodForConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member)
3967                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3968             if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind)) {
3969                 return getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member);
3970             } else if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsMethod(refKind)) {
3971                 return getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member, findBoundCallerLookup(member));
3972             } else if (refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3973                 return getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(defc, member);
3974             }
3975             // oops
3976             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad MethodHandle constant #"+member);
3977         }
3978 
3979         static ConcurrentHashMap<MemberName, DirectMethodHandle> LOOKASIDE_TABLE = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();
3980     }

3982     /**
3983      * Produces a method handle constructing arrays of a desired type,
3984      * as if by the {@code anewarray} bytecode.
3985      * The return type of the method handle will be the array type.
3986      * The type of its sole argument will be {@code int}, which specifies the size of the array.
3987      *
3988      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a negative
3989      * array size, a {@code NegativeArraySizeException} will be thrown.
3990      *
3991      * @param arrayClass an array type
3992      * @return a method handle which can create arrays of the given type
3993      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3994      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code arrayClass} is not an array type
3995      * @see java.lang.reflect.Array#newInstance(Class, int)
3996      * @jvms 6.5 {@code anewarray} Instruction
3997      * @since 9
3998      */
3999     public static MethodHandle arrayConstructor(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4000         if (!arrayClass.isArray()) {
4001             throw newIllegalArgumentException("not an array class: " + arrayClass.getName());
4002         }
4003         MethodHandle ani = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_Array_newInstance).
4004                 bindTo(arrayClass.getComponentType());
4005         return ani.asType(ani.type().changeReturnType(arrayClass));
4006     }

4079     /**
4080      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array of type
4081      * {@code arrayClass}.  The VarHandle's variable type is the component type
4082      * of {@code arrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4083      * {@code (arrayClass, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4084      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into an array.
4085      * <p>
4086      * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
4087      * the following conditions:
4088      * <ul>
4089      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code byte},
4090      *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
4091      *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update access
4092      *     modes are unsupported.
4093      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code boolean},
4094      *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
4095      *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
4096      *     unsupported.
4097      * </ul>
4098      * <p>
4099      * If the component type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
4100      * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
4101      * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4102      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4103      *
4104      * <p> When the returned {@code VarHandle} is invoked,
4105      * the array reference and array index are checked.
4106      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
4107      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
4108      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
4109      * the length of the array.
4110      *
4111      * @apiNote
4112      * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
4113      * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
4114      * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
4115      * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
4116      * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
4117      * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
4118      * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
4119      * unexpectedly fail.
4120      * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
4121      * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
4122      * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
4123      * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
4124      * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
4125      * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
4126      * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
4127      * details).
4128      * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
4129      * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
4130      * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
4131      * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
4132      * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
4133      * @param arrayClass the class of an array, of type {@code T[]}
4134      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array
4135      * @throws NullPointerException if the arrayClass is null
4136      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4137      * @since 9
4138      */
4139     public static VarHandle arrayElementVarHandle(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4140         return VarHandles.makeArrayElementHandle(arrayClass);
4141     }
4142 
4143     /**
4144      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4145      * viewed as if it were a different primitive array type, such as
4146      * {@code int[]} or {@code long[]}.
4147      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4148      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4149      * {@code (byte[], int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4150      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4151      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a {@code byte[]}
4152      * array, composing bytes to or from a value of the component type of
4153      * {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4154      * <p>
4155      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4156      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4157      * {@code double}.
4158      * <p>
4159      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4160      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4161      * or greater than the {@code byte[]} array length minus the size (in bytes)
4162      * of {@code T}.
4163      * <p>
4164      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4165      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4166      * with the array and index.
4167      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4168      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4169      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4170      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4171      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4172      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4173      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4174      * <ul>
4175      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4176      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4177      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4178      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4179      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4180      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4181      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4182      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4183      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4184      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4185      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4186      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4187      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4188      * </ul>
4189      * <p>
4190      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4191      * for {@code byte[]} arrays without operating on a specific array.  Given
4192      * an {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4193      * {@code T_BOX}, misalignment may be determined as follows:
4194      * <pre>{@code
4195      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4196      * int misalignedAtZeroIndex = ByteBuffer.wrap(new byte[0]).
4197      *     alignmentOffset(0, sizeOfT);
4198      * int misalignedAtIndex = (misalignedAtZeroIndex + index) % sizeOfT;
4199      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4200      * }</pre>
4201      * <p>
4202      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4203      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4204      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4205      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4206      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4207      * type {@code T}
4208      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4209      * stored in the underlying {@code byte} array
4210      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4211      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4212      * array class
4213      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4214      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4215      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4216      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4217      * @since 9
4218      */
4219     public static VarHandle byteArrayViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4220                                      ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4221         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4222         return VarHandles.byteArrayViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4223                                               byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4224     }
4225 
4226     /**
4227      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4228      * viewed as if it were an array of elements of a different primitive
4229      * component type to that of {@code byte}, such as {@code int[]} or
4230      * {@code long[]}.
4231      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4232      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4233      * {@code (ByteBuffer, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4234      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4235      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a
4236      * {@code ByteBuffer}, composing bytes to or from a value of the component
4237      * type of {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4238      * <p>
4239      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4240      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4241      * {@code double}.
4242      * <p>
4243      * Access will result in a {@code ReadOnlyBufferException} for anything
4244      * other than the read access modes if the {@code ByteBuffer} is read-only.
4245      * <p>
4246      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4247      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4248      * or greater than the {@code ByteBuffer} limit minus the size (in bytes) of
4249      * {@code T}.
4250      * <p>
4251      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4252      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4253      * with the {@code ByteBuffer} and index.
4254      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4255      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4256      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4257      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4258      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4259      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4260      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4261      * <ul>
4262      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4263      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4264      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4265      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4266      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4267      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4268      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4269      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4270      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4271      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4272      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4273      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4274      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4275      * </ul>
4276      * <p>
4277      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4278      * for a {@code ByteBuffer}, {@code bb} (direct or otherwise), an
4279      * {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4280      * {@code T_BOX}, as follows:
4281      * <pre>{@code
4282      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4283      * ByteBuffer bb = ...
4284      * int misalignedAtIndex = bb.alignmentOffset(index, sizeOfT);
4285      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4286      * }</pre>
4287      * <p>
4288      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4289      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4290      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4291      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4292      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4293      * type {@code T}
4294      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4295      * stored in the underlying {@code ByteBuffer} (Note this overrides the
4296      * endianness of a {@code ByteBuffer})
4297      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4298      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4299      * array class
4300      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4301      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4302      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4303      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4304      * @since 9
4305      */
4306     public static VarHandle byteBufferViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4307                                       ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4308         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4309         return VarHandles.makeByteBufferViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4310                                                    byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4311     }

4313 
4314     /// method handle invocation (reflective style)
4315 
4316     /**
4317      * Produces a method handle which will invoke any method handle of the
4318      * given {@code type}, with a given number of trailing arguments replaced by
4319      * a single trailing {@code Object[]} array.
4320      * The resulting invoker will be a method handle with the following
4321      * arguments:
4322      * <ul>
4323      * <li>a single {@code MethodHandle} target
4324      * <li>zero or more leading values (counted by {@code leadingArgCount})
4325      * <li>an {@code Object[]} array containing trailing arguments
4326      * </ul>
4327      * <p>
4328      * The invoker will invoke its target like a call to {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke} with
4329      * the indicated {@code type}.
4330      * That is, if the target is exactly of the given {@code type}, it will behave
4331      * like {@code invokeExact}; otherwise it behave as if {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}
4332      * is used to convert the target to the required {@code type}.
4333      * <p>
4334      * The type of the returned invoker will not be the given {@code type}, but rather
4335      * will have all parameters except the first {@code leadingArgCount}
4336      * replaced by a single array of type {@code Object[]}, which will be
4337      * the final parameter.
4338      * <p>
4339      * Before invoking its target, the invoker will spread the final array, apply
4340      * reference casts as necessary, and unbox and widen primitive arguments.
4341      * If, when the invoker is called, the supplied array argument does
4342      * not have the correct number of elements, the invoker will throw
4343      * an {@link IllegalArgumentException} instead of invoking the target.
4344      * <p>
4345      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4346      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4347 MethodHandle invoker = MethodHandles.invoker(type);
4348 int spreadArgCount = type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount;
4349 invoker = invoker.asSpreader(Object[].class, spreadArgCount);
4350 return invoker;
4351      * }</pre></blockquote>
4352      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4353      * @param type the desired target type
4354      * @param leadingArgCount number of fixed arguments, to be passed unchanged to the target
4355      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4356      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code type} is null
4357      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code leadingArgCount} is not in
4358      *                  the range from 0 to {@code type.parameterCount()} inclusive,
4359      *                  or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4360      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4361      */
4362     public static MethodHandle spreadInvoker(MethodType type, int leadingArgCount) {
4363         if (leadingArgCount < 0 || leadingArgCount > type.parameterCount())
4364             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad argument count", leadingArgCount);
4365         type = type.asSpreaderType(Object[].class, leadingArgCount, type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount);
4366         return type.invokers().spreadInvoker(leadingArgCount);
4367     }
4368 
4369     /**
4370      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4371      * invoke any method handle of the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invokeExact invokeExact}.
4372      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4373      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4374      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4375      * <p>
4376      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4377      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invokeExact", type)}
4378      *
4379      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4380      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4381      * Invoker method handles can be useful when working with variable method handles
4382      * of unknown types.
4383      * For example, to emulate an {@code invokeExact} call to a variable method
4384      * handle {@code M}, extract its type {@code T},
4385      * look up the invoker method {@code X} for {@code T},
4386      * and call the invoker method, as {@code X.invoke(T, A...)}.
4387      * (It would not work to call {@code X.invokeExact}, since the type {@code T}
4388      * is unknown.)
4389      * If spreading, collecting, or other argument transformations are required,
4390      * they can be applied once to the invoker {@code X} and reused on many {@code M}
4391      * method handle values, as long as they are compatible with the type of {@code X}.
4392      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4393      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4394      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4395      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4396      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4397      * <p>
4398      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4399      * @param type the desired target type
4400      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4401      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4402      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4403      */
4404     public static MethodHandle exactInvoker(MethodType type) {
4405         return type.invokers().exactInvoker();
4406     }
4407 
4408     /**
4409      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4410      * invoke any method handle compatible with the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke}.
4411      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4412      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4413      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4414      * <p>
4415      * Before invoking its target, if the target differs from the expected type,
4416      * the invoker will apply reference casts as
4417      * necessary and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4418      * Similarly, the return value will be converted as necessary.
4419      * If the target is a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity method handle},
4420      * the required arity conversion will be made, again as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4421      * <p>
4422      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4423      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invoke", type)}
4424      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4425      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4426      * A {@linkplain MethodType#genericMethodType general method type} is one which
4427      * mentions only {@code Object} arguments and return values.
4428      * An invoker for such a type is capable of calling any method handle
4429      * of the same arity as the general type.
4430      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4431      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4432      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4433      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4434      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4435      * <p>
4436      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4437      * @param type the desired target type
4438      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle convertible to the given type
4439      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4440      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4441      */
4442     public static MethodHandle invoker(MethodType type) {
4443         return type.invokers().genericInvoker();
4444     }
4445 
4446     /**
4447      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4448      * invoke a signature-polymorphic access mode method on any VarHandle whose
4449      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4450      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
4451      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
4452      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
4453      *
4454      * @param accessMode the VarHandle access mode
4455      * @param type the desired target type
4456      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking an access mode method of
4457      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is of the given type.
4458      * @since 9
4459      */
4460     public static MethodHandle varHandleExactInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {
4461         return type.invokers().varHandleMethodExactInvoker(accessMode);
4462     }
4463 
4464     /**
4465      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4466      * invoke a signature-polymorphic access mode method on any VarHandle whose
4467      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4468      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
4469      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
4470      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
4471      * <p>
4472      * Before invoking its target, if the access mode type differs from the
4473      * desired given type, the invoker will apply reference casts as necessary
4474      * and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by
4475      * {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.  Similarly, the return value will be
4476      * converted as necessary.
4477      * <p>
4478      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more
4479      * efficient): {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(VarHandle.class, accessMode.name(), type)}
4480      *
4481      * @param accessMode the VarHandle access mode
4482      * @param type the desired target type
4483      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking an access mode method of
4484      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is convertible to the given
4485      *         type.
4486      * @since 9
4487      */
4488     public static MethodHandle varHandleInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {
4489         return type.invokers().varHandleMethodInvoker(accessMode);
4490     }
4491 
4492     /*non-public*/
4493     static MethodHandle basicInvoker(MethodType type) {
4494         return type.invokers().basicInvoker();
4495     }
4496 
4497      /// method handle modification (creation from other method handles)
4498 
4499     /**
4500      * Produces a method handle which adapts the type of the
4501      * given method handle to a new type by pairwise argument and return type conversion.
4502      * The original type and new type must have the same number of arguments.
4503      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4504      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4505      * <p>
4506      * If the original type and new type are equal, returns target.
4507      * <p>
4508      * The same conversions are allowed as for {@link MethodHandle#asType MethodHandle.asType},
4509      * and some additional conversions are also applied if those conversions fail.
4510      * Given types <em>T0</em>, <em>T1</em>, one of the following conversions is applied
4511      * if possible, before or instead of any conversions done by {@code asType}:
4512      * <ul>
4513      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are references, and <em>T1</em> is an interface type,
4514      *     then the value of type <em>T0</em> is passed as a <em>T1</em> without a cast.
4515      *     (This treatment of interfaces follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4516      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is boolean and <em>T1</em> is another primitive,
4517      *     the boolean is converted to a byte value, 1 for true, 0 for false.
4518      *     (This treatment follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4519      * <li>If <em>T1</em> is boolean and <em>T0</em> is another primitive,
4520      *     <em>T0</em> is converted to byte via Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5),
4521      *     and the low order bit of the result is tested, as if by {@code (x & 1) != 0}.
4522      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are primitives other than boolean,
4523      *     then a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) is applied.
4524      *     (Specifically, <em>T0</em> will convert to <em>T1</em> by
4525      *     widening and/or narrowing.)
4526      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive, an unboxing
4527      *     conversion will be applied at runtime, possibly followed
4528      *     by a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) on the primitive value,
4529      *     possibly followed by a conversion from byte to boolean by testing
4530      *     the low-order bit.
4531      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive,
4532      *     and if the reference is null at runtime, a zero value is introduced.
4533      * </ul>
4534      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are retyped
4535      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4536      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after performing
4537      *           any necessary argument conversions, and arranges for any
4538      *           necessary return value conversions
4539      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4540      * @throws WrongMethodTypeException if the conversion cannot be made
4541      * @see MethodHandle#asType
4542      */
4543     public static MethodHandle explicitCastArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4544         explicitCastArgumentsChecks(target, newType);
4545         // use the asTypeCache when possible:
4546         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4547         if (oldType == newType)  return target;
4548         if (oldType.explicitCastEquivalentToAsType(newType)) {
4549             return target.asFixedArity().asType(newType);
4550         }
4551         return MethodHandleImpl.makePairwiseConvert(target, newType, false);
4552     }
4553 
4554     private static void explicitCastArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4555         if (target.type().parameterCount() != newType.parameterCount()) {
4556             throw new WrongMethodTypeException("cannot explicitly cast " + target + " to " + newType);
4557         }
4558     }
4559 
4560     /**
4561      * Produces a method handle which adapts the calling sequence of the
4562      * given method handle to a new type, by reordering the arguments.
4563      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4564      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4565      * <p>
4566      * The given array controls the reordering.
4567      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming parameters (the value
4568      * {@code newType.parameterCount()}, and call {@code #O} the number
4569      * of outgoing parameters (the value {@code target.type().parameterCount()}).
4570      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
4571      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
4572      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
4573      * outgoing argument will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
4574      * argument, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
4575      * <p>
4576      * No argument or return value conversions are applied.
4577      * The type of each incoming argument, as determined by {@code newType},
4578      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing parameter
4579      * or parameters in the target method handle.
4580      * The return type of {@code newType} must be identical to the return
4581      * type of the original target.
4582      * <p>
4583      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
4584      * An incoming argument will be duplicated if its index appears
4585      * more than once in the array, and an incoming argument will be dropped
4586      * if its index does not appear in the array.
4587      * As in the case of {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments},
4588      * incoming arguments which are not mentioned in the reordering array
4589      * may be of any type, as determined only by {@code newType}.
4590      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4591 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4592 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4593 ...
4594 MethodType intfn1 = methodType(int.class, int.class);
4595 MethodType intfn2 = methodType(int.class, int.class, int.class);
4596 MethodHandle sub = ... (int x, int y) -> (x-y) ...;
4597 assert(sub.type().equals(intfn2));
4598 MethodHandle sub1 = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 0, 1);
4599 MethodHandle rsub = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 1, 0);
4600 assert((int)rsub.invokeExact(1, 100) == 99);
4601 MethodHandle add = ... (int x, int y) -> (x+y) ...;
4602 assert(add.type().equals(intfn2));
4603 MethodHandle twice = permuteArguments(add, intfn1, 0, 0);
4604 assert(twice.type().equals(intfn1));
4605 assert((int)twice.invokeExact(21) == 42);
4606      * }</pre></blockquote>
4607      * <p>
4608      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4609      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4610      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are reordered
4611      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4612      * @param reorder an index array which controls the reordering
4613      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after it
4614      *           drops unused arguments and moves and/or duplicates the other arguments
4615      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
4616      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the index array length is not equal to
4617      *                  the arity of the target, or if any index array element
4618      *                  not a valid index for a parameter of {@code newType},
4619      *                  or if two corresponding parameter types in
4620      *                  {@code target.type()} and {@code newType} are not identical,
4621      */
4622     public static MethodHandle permuteArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType, int... reorder) {
4623         reorder = reorder.clone();  // get a private copy
4624         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4625         permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType);
4626         // first detect dropped arguments and handle them separately
4627         int[] originalReorder = reorder;
4628         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4629         LambdaForm form = result.form;
4630         int newArity = newType.parameterCount();
4631         // Normalize the reordering into a real permutation,
4632         // by removing duplicates and adding dropped elements.
4633         // This somewhat improves lambda form caching, as well
4634         // as simplifying the transform by breaking it up into steps.
4635         for (int ddIdx; (ddIdx = findFirstDupOrDrop(reorder, newArity)) != 0; ) {
4636             if (ddIdx > 0) {
4637                 // We found a duplicated entry at reorder[ddIdx].
4638                 // Example:  (x,y,z)->asList(x,y,z)
4639                 // permuted by [1*,0,1] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a1,a0,a1)
4640                 // permuted by [0,1,0*] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a0,a1,a0)
4641                 // The starred element corresponds to the argument
4642                 // deleted by the dupArgumentForm transform.
4643                 int srcPos = ddIdx, dstPos = srcPos, dupVal = reorder[srcPos];
4644                 boolean killFirst = false;
4645                 for (int val; (val = reorder[--dstPos]) != dupVal; ) {
4646                     // Set killFirst if the dup is larger than an intervening position.
4647                     // This will remove at least one inversion from the permutation.
4648                     if (dupVal > val) killFirst = true;
4649                 }
4650                 if (!killFirst) {
4651                     srcPos = dstPos;
4652                     dstPos = ddIdx;
4653                 }
4654                 form = form.editor().dupArgumentForm(1 + srcPos, 1 + dstPos);
4655                 assert (reorder[srcPos] == reorder[dstPos]);
4656                 oldType = oldType.dropParameterTypes(dstPos, dstPos + 1);
4657                 // contract the reordering by removing the element at dstPos
4658                 int tailPos = dstPos + 1;
4659                 System.arraycopy(reorder, tailPos, reorder, dstPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4660                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length - 1);
4661             } else {
4662                 int dropVal = ~ddIdx, insPos = 0;
4663                 while (insPos < reorder.length && reorder[insPos] < dropVal) {
4664                     // Find first element of reorder larger than dropVal.
4665                     // This is where we will insert the dropVal.
4666                     insPos += 1;
4667                 }
4668                 Class<?> ptype = newType.parameterType(dropVal);
4669                 form = form.editor().addArgumentForm(1 + insPos, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4670                 oldType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(insPos, ptype);
4671                 // expand the reordering by inserting an element at insPos
4672                 int tailPos = insPos + 1;
4673                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length + 1);
4674                 System.arraycopy(reorder, insPos, reorder, tailPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4675                 reorder[insPos] = dropVal;
4676             }
4677             assert (permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType));
4678         }
4679         assert (reorder.length == newArity);  // a perfect permutation
4680         // Note:  This may cache too many distinct LFs. Consider backing off to varargs code.
4681         form = form.editor().permuteArgumentsForm(1, reorder);
4682         if (newType == result.type() && form == result.internalForm())
4683             return result;
4684         return result.copyWith(newType, form);
4685     }
4686 
4687     /**
4688      * Return an indication of any duplicate or omission in reorder.
4689      * If the reorder contains a duplicate entry, return the index of the second occurrence.
4690      * Otherwise, return ~(n), for the first n in [0..newArity-1] that is not present in reorder.
4691      * Otherwise, return zero.
4692      * If an element not in [0..newArity-1] is encountered, return reorder.length.
4693      */
4694     private static int findFirstDupOrDrop(int[] reorder, int newArity) {
4695         final int BIT_LIMIT = 63;  // max number of bits in bit mask
4696         if (newArity < BIT_LIMIT) {
4697             long mask = 0;
4698             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4699                 int arg = reorder[i];
