4700                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4701                     return reorder.length;
4702                 }
4703                 long bit = 1L << arg;
4704                 if ((mask & bit) != 0) {
4705                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4706                 }
4707                 mask |= bit;
4708             }
4709             if (mask == (1L << newArity) - 1) {
4710                 assert(Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(Long.lowestOneBit(~mask)) == newArity);
4711                 return 0;
4712             }
4713             // find first zero
4714             long zeroBit = Long.lowestOneBit(~mask);
4715             int zeroPos = Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(zeroBit);
4716             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4717             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4718                 return 0;
4719             }
4720             return ~zeroPos;
4721         } else {
4722             // same algorithm, different bit set
4723             BitSet mask = new BitSet(newArity);
4724             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4725                 int arg = reorder[i];
4726                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4727                     return reorder.length;
4728                 }
4729                 if (mask.get(arg)) {
4730                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4731                 }
4732                 mask.set(arg);
4733             }
4734             int zeroPos = mask.nextClearBit(0);
4735             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4736             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4737                 return 0;
4738             }
4739             return ~zeroPos;
4740         }
4741     }
4742 
4743     static boolean permuteArgumentChecks(int[] reorder, MethodType newType, MethodType oldType) {
4744         if (newType.returnType() != oldType.returnType())
4745             throw newIllegalArgumentException("return types do not match",
4746                     oldType, newType);
4747         if (reorder.length == oldType.parameterCount()) {
4748             int limit = newType.parameterCount();
4749             boolean bad = false;
4750             for (int j = 0; j < reorder.length; j++) {
4751                 int i = reorder[j];
4752                 if (i < 0 || i >= limit) {
4753                     bad = true; break;
4754                 }
4755                 Class<?> src = newType.parameterType(i);
4756                 Class<?> dst = oldType.parameterType(j);
4757                 if (src != dst)
4758                     throw newIllegalArgumentException("parameter types do not match after reorder",
4759                             oldType, newType);
4760             }
4761             if (!bad)  return true;
4762         }
4763         throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad reorder array: "+Arrays.toString(reorder));
4764     }
4765 
4766     /**
4767      * Produces a method handle of the requested return type which returns the given
4768      * constant value every time it is invoked.
4769      * <p>
4770      * Before the method handle is returned, the passed-in value is converted to the requested type.
4771      * If the requested type is primitive, widening primitive conversions are attempted,
4772      * else reference conversions are attempted.
4773      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code identity(type).bindTo(value)}.
4774      * @param type the return type of the desired method handle
4775      * @param value the value to return
4776      * @return a method handle of the given return type and no arguments, which always returns the given value
4777      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code type} argument is null
4778      * @throws ClassCastException if the value cannot be converted to the required return type
4779      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4780      */
4781     public static MethodHandle constant(Class<?> type, Object value) {
4782         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4783             if (type == void.class)
4784                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("void type");
4785             Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type);
4786             value = w.convert(value, type);
4787             if (w.zero().equals(value))
4788                 return zero(w, type);
4789             return insertArguments(identity(type), 0, value);
4790         } else {
4791             if (value == null)
4792                 return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4793             return identity(type).bindTo(value);
4794         }
4795     }
4796 
4797     /**
4798      * Produces a method handle which returns its sole argument when invoked.
4799      * @param type the type of the sole parameter and return value of the desired method handle
4800      * @return a unary method handle which accepts and returns the given type
4801      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4802      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4803      */
4804     public static MethodHandle identity(Class<?> type) {
4805         Wrapper btw = (type.isPrimitive() ? Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type) : Wrapper.OBJECT);
4806         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4807         MethodHandle ident = IDENTITY_MHS[pos];
4808         if (ident == null) {
4809             ident = setCachedMethodHandle(IDENTITY_MHS, pos, makeIdentity(btw.primitiveType()));
4810         }
4811         if (ident.type().returnType() == type)
4812             return ident;
4813         // something like identity(Foo.class); do not bother to intern these
4814         assert (btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4815         return makeIdentity(type);
4816     }
4817 
4818     /**
4819      * Produces a constant method handle of the requested return type which
4820      * returns the default value for that type every time it is invoked.
4821      * The resulting constant method handle will have no side effects.
4822      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code empty(methodType(type))}.
4823      * It is also equivalent to {@code explicitCastArguments(constant(Object.class, null), methodType(type))},
4824      * since {@code explicitCastArguments} converts {@code null} to default values.
4825      * @param type the expected return type of the desired method handle
4826      * @return a constant method handle that takes no arguments
4827      *         and returns the default value of the given type (or void, if the type is void)
4828      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4829      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4830      * @see MethodHandles#empty
4831      * @see MethodHandles#explicitCastArguments
4832      * @since 9
4833      */
4834     public static MethodHandle zero(Class<?> type) {
4835         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4836         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4837             return zero(Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type), type);
4838         } else if (type.isInlineClass()) {
4839             throw new UnsupportedOperationException();
4840         } else {
4841             return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4842         }
4843     }
4844 
4845     private static MethodHandle identityOrVoid(Class<?> type) {
4846         return type == void.class ? zero(type) : identity(type);
4847     }
4848 
4849     /**
4850      * Produces a method handle of the requested type which ignores any arguments, does nothing,
4851      * and returns a suitable default depending on the return type.
4852      * That is, it returns a zero primitive value, a {@code null}, or {@code void}.
4853      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to
4854      * {@code dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList())}.
4855      *
4856      * @apiNote Given a predicate and target, a useful "if-then" construct can be produced as
4857      * {@code guardWithTest(pred, target, empty(target.type())}.
4858      * @param type the type of the desired method handle
4859      * @return a constant method handle of the given type, which returns a default value of the given return type
4860      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4861      * @see MethodHandles#zero
4862      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4863      * @since 9
4864      */
4865     public static  MethodHandle empty(MethodType type) {
4866         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4867         return dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList());
4868     }
4869 
4870     private static final MethodHandle[] IDENTITY_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4871     private static MethodHandle makeIdentity(Class<?> ptype) {
4872         MethodType mtype = MethodType.methodType(ptype, ptype);
4873         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.identityForm(BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4874         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.IDENTITY);
4875     }
4876 
4877     private static MethodHandle zero(Wrapper btw, Class<?> rtype) {
4878         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4879         MethodHandle zero = ZERO_MHS[pos];
4880         if (zero == null) {
4881             zero = setCachedMethodHandle(ZERO_MHS, pos, makeZero(btw.primitiveType()));
4882         }
4883         if (zero.type().returnType() == rtype)
4884             return zero;
4885         assert(btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4886         return makeZero(rtype);
4887     }
4888     private static final MethodHandle[] ZERO_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4889     private static MethodHandle makeZero(Class<?> rtype) {
4890         MethodType mtype = methodType(rtype);
4891         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.zeroForm(BasicType.basicType(rtype));
4892         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.ZERO);
4893     }
4894 
4895     private static synchronized MethodHandle setCachedMethodHandle(MethodHandle[] cache, int pos, MethodHandle value) {
4896         // Simulate a CAS, to avoid racy duplication of results.
4897         MethodHandle prev = cache[pos];
4898         if (prev != null) return prev;
4899         return cache[pos] = value;
4900     }
4901 
4902     /**
4903      * Provides a target method handle with one or more <em>bound arguments</em>
4904      * in advance of the method handle's invocation.
4905      * The formal parameters to the target corresponding to the bound
4906      * arguments are called <em>bound parameters</em>.
4907      * Returns a new method handle which saves away the bound arguments.
4908      * When it is invoked, it receives arguments for any non-bound parameters,
4909      * binds the saved arguments to their corresponding parameters,
4910      * and calls the original target.
4911      * <p>
4912      * The type of the new method handle will drop the types for the bound
4913      * parameters from the original target type, since the new method handle
4914      * will no longer require those arguments to be supplied by its callers.
4915      * <p>
4916      * Each given argument object must match the corresponding bound parameter type.
4917      * If a bound parameter type is a primitive, the argument object
4918      * must be a wrapper, and will be unboxed to produce the primitive value.
4919      * <p>
4920      * The {@code pos} argument selects which parameters are to be bound.
4921      * It may range between zero and <i>N-L</i> (inclusively),
4922      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target method handle
4923      * and <i>L</i> is the length of the values array.
4924      * <p>
4925      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4926      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4927      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the argument is inserted
4928      * @param pos where to insert the argument (zero for the first)
4929      * @param values the series of arguments to insert
4930      * @return a method handle which inserts an additional argument,
4931      *         before calling the original method handle
4932      * @throws NullPointerException if the target or the {@code values} array is null
4933      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if (@code pos) is less than {@code 0} or greater than
4934      *         {@code N - L} where {@code N} is the arity of the target method handle and {@code L}
4935      *         is the length of the values array.
4936      * @throws ClassCastException if an argument does not match the corresponding bound parameter
4937      *         type.
4938      * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
4939      */
4940     public static MethodHandle insertArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Object... values) {
4941         int insCount = values.length;
4942         Class<?>[] ptypes = insertArgumentsChecks(target, insCount, pos);
4943         if (insCount == 0)  return target;
4944         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4945         for (int i = 0; i < insCount; i++) {
4946             Object value = values[i];
4947             Class<?> ptype = ptypes[pos+i];
4948             if (ptype.isPrimitive()) {
4949                 result = insertArgumentPrimitive(result, pos, ptype, value);
4950             } else {
4951                 value = ptype.cast(value);  // throw CCE if needed
4952                 result = result.bindArgumentL(pos, value);
4953             }
4954         }
4955         return result;
4956     }
4957 
4958     private static BoundMethodHandle insertArgumentPrimitive(BoundMethodHandle result, int pos,
4959                                                              Class<?> ptype, Object value) {
4960         Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(ptype);
4961         // perform unboxing and/or primitive conversion
4962         value = w.convert(value, ptype);
4963         switch (w) {
4964         case INT:     return result.bindArgumentI(pos, (int)value);
4965         case LONG:    return result.bindArgumentJ(pos, (long)value);
4966         case FLOAT:   return result.bindArgumentF(pos, (float)value);
4967         case DOUBLE:  return result.bindArgumentD(pos, (double)value);
4968         default:      return result.bindArgumentI(pos, ValueConversions.widenSubword(value));
4969         }
4970     }
4971 
4972     private static Class<?>[] insertArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int insCount, int pos) throws RuntimeException {
4973         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4974         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4975         int inargs  = outargs - insCount;
4976         if (inargs < 0)
4977             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many values to insert");
4978         if (pos < 0 || pos > inargs)
4979             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to append");
4980         return oldType.ptypes();
4981     }
4982 
4983     /**
4984      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4985      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4986      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4987      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4988      * at some given position.
4989      * <p>
4990      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4991      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4992      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4993      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4994      * they will come after.
4995      * <p>
4996      * <b>Example:</b>
4997      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4998 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4999 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5000 ...
5001 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5002   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5003 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5004 MethodType bigType = cat.type().insertParameterTypes(0, int.class, String.class);
5005 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, bigType.parameterList().subList(0,2));
5006 assertEquals(bigType, d0.type());
5007 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact(123, "x", "y", "z"));
5008      * }</pre></blockquote>
5009      * <p>
5010      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
5011      * <blockquote><pre>
5012      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,Class...) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, valueTypes.toArray(new Class[0]))}
5013      * </pre></blockquote>
5014      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
5015      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
5016      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
5017      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
5018      *         before calling the original method handle
5019      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
5020      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} list or any of its elements is null
5021      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
5022      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5023      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have too many parameters
5024      */
5025     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
5026         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes.toArray()));
5027     }
5028 
5029     private static List<Class<?>> copyTypes(Object[] array) {
5030         return Arrays.asList(Arrays.copyOf(array, array.length, Class[].class));
5031     }
5032 
5033     private static MethodHandle dropArguments0(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
5034         MethodType oldType = target.type();  // get NPE
5035         int dropped = dropArgumentChecks(oldType, pos, valueTypes);
5036         MethodType newType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(pos, valueTypes);
5037         if (dropped == 0)  return target;
5038         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5039         LambdaForm lform = result.form;
5040         int insertFormArg = 1 + pos;
5041         for (Class<?> ptype : valueTypes) {
5042             lform = lform.editor().addArgumentForm(insertFormArg++, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
5043         }
5044         result = result.copyWith(newType, lform);
5045         return result;
5046     }
5047 
5048     private static int dropArgumentChecks(MethodType oldType, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
5049         int dropped = valueTypes.size();
5050         MethodType.checkSlotCount(dropped);
5051         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
5052         int inargs  = outargs + dropped;
5053         if (pos < 0 || pos > outargs)
5054             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to remove"
5055                     + Arrays.asList(oldType, pos, valueTypes, inargs, outargs)
5056                     );
5057         return dropped;
5058     }
5059 
5060     /**
5061      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
5062      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
5063      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
5064      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
5065      * at some given position.
5066      * <p>
5067      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
5068      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
5069      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
5070      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
5071      * they will come after.
5072      * @apiNote
5073      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5074 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5075 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5076 ...
5077 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5078   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5079 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5080 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, String.class);
5081 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5082 MethodHandle d1 = dropArguments(cat, 1, String.class);
5083 assertEquals("xz", (String) d1.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5084 MethodHandle d2 = dropArguments(cat, 2, String.class);
5085 assertEquals("xy", (String) d2.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5086 MethodHandle d12 = dropArguments(cat, 1, int.class, boolean.class);
5087 assertEquals("xz", (String) d12.invokeExact("x", 12, true, "z"));
5088      * }</pre></blockquote>
5089      * <p>
5090      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
5091      * <blockquote><pre>
5092      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, Arrays.asList(valueTypes))}
5093      * </pre></blockquote>
5094      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
5095      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
5096      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
5097      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
5098      *         before calling the original method handle
5099      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
5100      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} array or any of its elements is null
5101      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
5102      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5103      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have
5104      *                  <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5105      */
5106     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Class<?>... valueTypes) {
5107         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes));
5108     }
5109 
5110     // private version which allows caller some freedom with error handling
5111     private static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos,
5112                                       boolean nullOnFailure) {
5113         newTypes = copyTypes(newTypes.toArray());
5114         List<Class<?>> oldTypes = target.type().parameterList();
5115         int match = oldTypes.size();
5116         if (skip != 0) {
5117             if (skip < 0 || skip > match) {
5118                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal skip", skip, target);
5119             }
5120             oldTypes = oldTypes.subList(skip, match);
5121             match -= skip;
5122         }
5123         List<Class<?>> addTypes = newTypes;
5124         int add = addTypes.size();
5125         if (pos != 0) {
5126             if (pos < 0 || pos > add) {
5127                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal pos", pos, newTypes);
5128             }
5129             addTypes = addTypes.subList(pos, add);
5130             add -= pos;
5131             assert(addTypes.size() == add);
5132         }
5133         // Do not add types which already match the existing arguments.
5134         if (match > add || !oldTypes.equals(addTypes.subList(0, match))) {
5135             if (nullOnFailure) {
5136                 return null;
5137             }
5138             throw newIllegalArgumentException("argument lists do not match", oldTypes, newTypes);
5139         }
5140         addTypes = addTypes.subList(match, add);
5141         add -= match;
5142         assert(addTypes.size() == add);
5143         // newTypes:     (   P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5144         // target: ( S*[skip],        M*[match]  )
5145         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5146         if (add > 0) {
5147             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip+ match, addTypes);
5148         }
5149         // adapter: (S*[skip],        M*[match], A*[add] )
5150         if (pos > 0) {
5151             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip, newTypes.subList(0, pos));
5152         }
5153         // adapter: (S*[skip], P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5154         return adapter;
5155     }
5156 
5157     /**
5158      * Adapts a target method handle to match the given parameter type list. If necessary, adds dummy arguments. Some
5159      * leading parameters can be skipped before matching begins. The remaining types in the {@code target}'s parameter
5160      * type list must be a sub-list of the {@code newTypes} type list at the starting position {@code pos}. The
5161      * resulting handle will have the target handle's parameter type list, with any non-matching parameter types (before
5162      * or after the matching sub-list) inserted in corresponding positions of the target's original parameters, as if by
5163      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5164      * <p>
5165      * The resulting handle will have the same return type as the target handle.
5166      * <p>
5167      * In more formal terms, assume these two type lists:<ul>
5168      * <li>The target handle has the parameter type list {@code S..., M...}, with as many types in {@code S} as
5169      * indicated by {@code skip}. The {@code M} types are those that are supposed to match part of the given type list,
5170      * {@code newTypes}.
5171      * <li>The {@code newTypes} list contains types {@code P..., M..., A...}, with as many types in {@code P} as
5172      * indicated by {@code pos}. The {@code M} types are precisely those that the {@code M} types in the target handle's
5173      * parameter type list are supposed to match. The types in {@code A} are additional types found after the matching
5174      * sub-list.
5175      * </ul>
5176      * Given these assumptions, the result of an invocation of {@code dropArgumentsToMatch} will have the parameter type
5177      * list {@code S..., P..., M..., A...}, with the {@code P} and {@code A} types inserted as if by
5178      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5179      *
5180      * @apiNote
5181      * Two method handles whose argument lists are "effectively identical" (i.e., identical in a common prefix) may be
5182      * mutually converted to a common type by two calls to {@code dropArgumentsToMatch}, as follows:
5183      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5184 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5185 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5186 ...
5187 ...
5188 MethodHandle h0 = constant(boolean.class, true);
5189 MethodHandle h1 = lookup().findVirtual(String.class, "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5190 MethodType bigType = h1.type().insertParameterTypes(1, String.class, int.class);
5191 MethodHandle h2 = dropArguments(h1, 0, bigType.parameterList());
5192 if (h1.type().parameterCount() < h2.type().parameterCount())
5193     h1 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h1, 0, h2.type().parameterList(), 0);  // lengthen h1
5194 else
5195     h2 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h2, 0, h1.type().parameterList(), 0);    // lengthen h2
5196 MethodHandle h3 = guardWithTest(h0, h1, h2);
5197 assertEquals("xy", h3.invoke("x", "y", 1, "a", "b", "c"));
5198      * }</pre></blockquote>
5199      * @param target the method handle to adapt
5200      * @param skip number of targets parameters to disregard (they will be unchanged)
5201      * @param newTypes the list of types to match {@code target}'s parameter type list to
5202      * @param pos place in {@code newTypes} where the non-skipped target parameters must occur
5203      * @return a possibly adapted method handle
5204      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5205      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code newTypes} is {@code void.class},
5206      *         or if {@code skip} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5207      *         or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the newTypes list size,
5208      *         or if {@code newTypes} does not contain the {@code target}'s non-skipped parameter types at position
5209      *         {@code pos}.
5210      * @since 9
5211      */
5212     public static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos) {
5213         Objects.requireNonNull(target);
5214         Objects.requireNonNull(newTypes);
5215         return dropArgumentsToMatch(target, skip, newTypes, pos, false);
5216     }
5217 
5218     /**
5219      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5220      * one or more of its arguments, each with its own unary filter function,
5221      * and then calling the target with each pre-processed argument
5222      * replaced by the result of its corresponding filter function.
5223      * <p>
5224      * The pre-processing is performed by one or more method handles,
5225      * specified in the elements of the {@code filters} array.
5226      * The first element of the filter array corresponds to the {@code pos}
5227      * argument of the target, and so on in sequence.
5228      * The filter functions are invoked in left to right order.
5229      * <p>
5230      * Null arguments in the array are treated as identity functions,
5231      * and the corresponding arguments left unchanged.
5232      * (If there are no non-null elements in the array, the original target is returned.)
5233      * Each filter is applied to the corresponding argument of the adapter.
5234      * <p>
5235      * If a filter {@code F} applies to the {@code N}th argument of
5236      * the target, then {@code F} must be a method handle which
5237      * takes exactly one argument.  The type of {@code F}'s sole argument
5238      * replaces the corresponding argument type of the target
5239      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5240      * The return type of {@code F} must be identical to the corresponding
5241      * parameter type of the target.
5242      * <p>
5243      * It is an error if there are elements of {@code filters}
5244      * (null or not)
5245      * which do not correspond to argument positions in the target.
5246      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5247      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5248 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5249 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5250 ...
5251 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5252   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5253 MethodHandle upcase = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5254   "toUpperCase", methodType(String.class));
5255 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5256 MethodHandle f0 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase);
5257 assertEquals("Xy", (String) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // Xy
5258 MethodHandle f1 = filterArguments(cat, 1, upcase);
5259 assertEquals("xY", (String) f1.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xY
5260 MethodHandle f2 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase, upcase);
5261 assertEquals("XY", (String) f2.invokeExact("x", "y")); // XY
5262      * }</pre></blockquote>
5263      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5264      * denotes the return type of both the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5265      * {@code P}/{@code p} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values
5266      * of the parameters and arguments that precede and follow the filter position
5267      * {@code pos}, respectively. {@code A[i]}/{@code a[i]} stand for the types and
5268      * values of the filtered parameters and arguments; they also represent the
5269      * return types of the {@code filter[i]} handles. The latter accept arguments
5270      * {@code v[i]} of type {@code V[i]}, which also appear in the signature of
5271      * the resulting adapter.
5272      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5273      * T target(P... p, A[i]... a[i], B... b);
5274      * A[i] filter[i](V[i]);
5275      * T adapter(P... p, V[i]... v[i], B... b) {
5276      *   return target(p..., filter[i](v[i])..., b...);
5277      * }
5278      * }</pre></blockquote>
5279      * <p>
5280      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5281      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5282      *
5283      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are filtered
5284      * @param pos the position of the first argument to filter
5285      * @param filters method handles to call initially on filtered arguments
5286      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument filtering logic
5287      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null
5288      *                              or if the {@code filters} array is null
5289      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if a non-null element of {@code filters}
5290      *          does not match a corresponding argument type of target as described above,
5291      *          or if the {@code pos+filters.length} is greater than {@code target.type().parameterCount()},
5292      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5293      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5294      */
5295     public static MethodHandle filterArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle... filters) {
5296         // In method types arguments start at index 0, while the LF
5297         // editor have the MH receiver at position 0 - adjust appropriately.
5298         final int MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET = 1;
5299         filterArgumentsCheckArity(target, pos, filters);
5300         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5301 
5302         // keep track of currently matched filters, as to optimize repeated filters
5303         int index = 0;
5304         int[] positions = new int[filters.length];
5305         MethodHandle filter = null;
5306 
5307         // process filters in reverse order so that the invocation of
5308         // the resulting adapter will invoke the filters in left-to-right order
5309         for (int i = filters.length - 1; i >= 0; --i) {
5310             MethodHandle newFilter = filters[i];
5311             if (newFilter == null) continue;  // ignore null elements of filters
5312 
5313             // flush changes on update
5314             if (filter != newFilter) {
5315                 if (filter != null) {
5316                     if (index > 1) {
5317                         adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5318                     } else {
5319                         adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5320                     }
5321                 }
5322                 filter = newFilter;
5323                 index = 0;
5324             }
5325 
5326             filterArgumentChecks(target, pos + i, newFilter);
5327             positions[index++] = pos + i + MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET;
5328         }
5329         if (index > 1) {
5330             adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5331         } else if (index == 1) {
5332             adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5333         }
5334         return adapter;
5335     }
5336 
5337     private static MethodHandle filterRepeatedArgument(MethodHandle adapter, MethodHandle filter, int[] positions) {
5338         MethodType targetType = adapter.type();
5339         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5340         BoundMethodHandle result = adapter.rebind();
5341         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5342 
5343         Class<?>[] ptypes = targetType.ptypes().clone();
5344         for (int pos : positions) {
5345             ptypes[pos - 1] = newParamType;
5346         }
5347         MethodType newType = MethodType.makeImpl(targetType.rtype(), ptypes, true);
5348 
5349         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterRepeatedArgumentForm(BasicType.basicType(newParamType), positions);
5350         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5351     }
5352 
5353     /*non-public*/
5354     static MethodHandle filterArgument(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5355         filterArgumentChecks(target, pos, filter);
5356         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5357         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5358         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5359         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5360         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterArgumentForm(1 + pos, BasicType.basicType(newParamType));
5361         MethodType newType = targetType.changeParameterType(pos, newParamType);
5362         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5363         return result;
5364     }
5365 
5366     private static void filterArgumentsCheckArity(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle[] filters) {
5367         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5368         int maxPos = targetType.parameterCount();
5369         if (pos + filters.length > maxPos)
5370             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many filters");
5371     }
5372 
5373     private static void filterArgumentChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5374         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5375         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5376         if (filterType.parameterCount() != 1
5377             || filterType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(pos))
5378             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5379     }
5380 
5381     /**
5382      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5383      * a sub-sequence of its arguments with a filter (another method handle).
5384      * The pre-processed arguments are replaced by the result (if any) of the
5385      * filter function.
5386      * The target is then called on the modified (usually shortened) argument list.
5387      * <p>
5388      * If the filter returns a value, the target must accept that value as
5389      * its argument in position {@code pos}, preceded and/or followed by
5390      * any arguments not passed to the filter.
5391      * If the filter returns void, the target must accept all arguments
5392      * not passed to the filter.
5393      * No arguments are reordered, and a result returned from the filter
5394      * replaces (in order) the whole subsequence of arguments originally
5395      * passed to the adapter.
5396      * <p>
5397      * The argument types (if any) of the filter
5398      * replace zero or one argument types of the target, at position {@code pos},
5399      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5400      * The return type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5401      * argument type of the target at position {@code pos}, and that target argument
5402      * is supplied by the return value of the filter.
5403      * <p>
5404      * In all cases, {@code pos} must be greater than or equal to zero, and
5405      * {@code pos} must also be less than or equal to the target's arity.
5406      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5407      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5408 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5409 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5410 ...
5411 MethodHandle deepToString = publicLookup()
5412   .findStatic(Arrays.class, "deepToString", methodType(String.class, Object[].class));
5413 
5414 MethodHandle ts1 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 1);
5415 assertEquals("[strange]", (String) ts1.invokeExact("strange"));
5416 
5417 MethodHandle ts2 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 2);
5418 assertEquals("[up, down]", (String) ts2.invokeExact("up", "down"));
5419 
5420 MethodHandle ts3 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 3);
5421 MethodHandle ts3_ts2 = collectArguments(ts3, 1, ts2);
5422 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], strange]",
5423              (String) ts3_ts2.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5424 
5425 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts1 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 3, ts1);
5426 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], [strange]]",
5427              (String) ts3_ts2_ts1.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5428 
5429 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts3 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 1, ts3);
5430 assertEquals("[top, [[up, down, strange], charm], bottom]",
5431              (String) ts3_ts2_ts3.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange", "charm", "bottom"));
5432      * }</pre></blockquote>
5433      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5434      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5435      * {@code V}/{@code v} stand for the return type and value of the
5436      * {@code filter}, which are also found in the signature and arguments of
5437      * the {@code target}, respectively, unless {@code V} is {@code void}.
5438      * {@code A}/{@code a} and {@code C}/{@code c} represent the parameter types
5439      * and values preceding and following the collection position, {@code pos},
5440      * in the {@code target}'s signature. They also turn up in the resulting
5441      * adapter's signature and arguments, where they surround
5442      * {@code B}/{@code b}, which represent the parameter types and arguments
5443      * to the {@code filter} (if any).
5444      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5445      * T target(A...,V,C...);
5446      * V filter(B...);
5447      * T adapter(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5448      *   V v = filter(b...);
5449      *   return target(a...,v,c...);
5450      * }
5451      * // and if the filter has no arguments:
5452      * T target2(A...,V,C...);
5453      * V filter2();
5454      * T adapter2(A... a,C... c) {
5455      *   V v = filter2();
5456      *   return target2(a...,v,c...);
5457      * }
5458      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5459      * T target3(A...,C...);
5460      * void filter3(B...);
5461      * T adapter3(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5462      *   filter3(b...);
5463      *   return target3(a...,c...);
5464      * }
5465      * }</pre></blockquote>
5466      * <p>
5467      * A collection adapter {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)} is equivalent to
5468      * one which first "folds" the affected arguments, and then drops them, in separate
5469      * steps as follows:
5470      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5471      * mh = MethodHandles.dropArguments(mh, 1, coll.type().parameterList()); //step 2
5472      * mh = MethodHandles.foldArguments(mh, coll); //step 1
5473      * }</pre></blockquote>
5474      * If the target method handle consumes no arguments besides than the result
5475      * (if any) of the filter {@code coll}, then {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)}
5476      * is equivalent to {@code filterReturnValue(coll, mh)}.
5477      * If the filter method handle {@code coll} consumes one argument and produces
5478      * a non-void result, then {@code collectArguments(mh, N, coll)}
5479      * is equivalent to {@code filterArguments(mh, N, coll)}.
5480      * Other equivalences are possible but would require argument permutation.
5481      * <p>
5482      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5483      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5484      *
5485      * @param target the method handle to invoke after filtering the subsequence of arguments
5486      * @param pos the position of the first adapter argument to pass to the filter,
5487      *            and/or the target argument which receives the result of the filter
5488      * @param filter method handle to call on the subsequence of arguments
5489      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument subsequence filtering logic
5490      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5491      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the return type of {@code filter}
5492      *          is non-void and is not the same as the {@code pos} argument of the target,
5493      *          or if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target's arity, inclusive,
5494      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5495      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5496      * @see MethodHandles#foldArguments
5497      * @see MethodHandles#filterArguments
5498      * @see MethodHandles#filterReturnValue
5499      */
5500     public static MethodHandle collectArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5501         MethodType newType = collectArgumentsChecks(target, pos, filter);
5502         MethodType collectorType = filter.type();
5503         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5504         LambdaForm lform;
5505         if (collectorType.returnType().isArray() && filter.intrinsicName() == Intrinsic.NEW_ARRAY) {
5506             lform = result.editor().collectArgumentArrayForm(1 + pos, filter);
5507             if (lform != null) {
5508                 return result.copyWith(newType, lform);
5509             }
5510         }
5511         lform = result.editor().collectArgumentsForm(1 + pos, collectorType.basicType());
5512         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5513     }
5514 
5515     private static MethodType collectArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5516         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5517         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5518         Class<?> rtype = filterType.returnType();
5519         List<Class<?>> filterArgs = filterType.parameterList();
5520         if (rtype == void.class) {
5521             return targetType.insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5522         }
5523         if (rtype != targetType.parameterType(pos)) {
5524             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5525         }
5526         return targetType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos+1).insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5527     }
5528 
5529     /**
5530      * Adapts a target method handle by post-processing
5531      * its return value (if any) with a filter (another method handle).
5532      * The result of the filter is returned from the adapter.
5533      * <p>
5534      * If the target returns a value, the filter must accept that value as
5535      * its only argument.
5536      * If the target returns void, the filter must accept no arguments.
5537      * <p>
5538      * The return type of the filter
5539      * replaces the return type of the target
5540      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5541      * The argument type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5542      * return type of the target.
5543      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5544      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5545 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5546 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5547 ...
5548 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5549   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5550 MethodHandle length = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5551   "length", methodType(int.class));
5552 System.out.println((String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xy
5553 MethodHandle f0 = filterReturnValue(cat, length);
5554 System.out.println((int) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // 2
5555      * }</pre></blockquote>
5556      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code,
5557      * {@code T}/{@code t} represent the result type and value of the
5558      * {@code target}; {@code V}, the result type of the {@code filter}; and
5559      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the parameters and arguments
5560      * of the {@code target} as well as the resulting adapter.
5561      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5562      * T target(A...);
5563      * V filter(T);
5564      * V adapter(A... a) {
5565      *   T t = target(a...);
5566      *   return filter(t);
5567      * }
5568      * // and if the target has a void return:
5569      * void target2(A...);
5570      * V filter2();
5571      * V adapter2(A... a) {
5572      *   target2(a...);
5573      *   return filter2();
5574      * }
5575      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5576      * T target3(A...);
5577      * void filter3(V);
5578      * void adapter3(A... a) {
5579      *   T t = target3(a...);
5580      *   filter3(t);
5581      * }
5582      * }</pre></blockquote>
5583      * <p>
5584      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5585      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5586      * @param target the method handle to invoke before filtering the return value
5587      * @param filter method handle to call on the return value
5588      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified return value filtering logic
5589      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5590      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the argument list of {@code filter}
5591      *          does not match the return type of target as described above
5592      */
5593     public static MethodHandle filterReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
5594         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5595         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5596         filterReturnValueChecks(targetType, filterType);
5597         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5598         BasicType rtype = BasicType.basicType(filterType.returnType());
5599         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterReturnForm(rtype, false);
5600         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
5601         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5602         return result;
5603     }
5604 
5605     private static void filterReturnValueChecks(MethodType targetType, MethodType filterType) throws RuntimeException {
5606         Class<?> rtype = targetType.returnType();
5607         int filterValues = filterType.parameterCount();
5608         if (filterValues == 0
5609                 ? (rtype != void.class)
5610                 : (rtype != filterType.parameterType(0) || filterValues != 1))
5611             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5612     }
5613 
5614     /**
5615      * Filter the return value of a target method handle with a filter function. The filter function is
5616      * applied to the return value of the original handle; if the filter specifies more than one parameters,
5617      * then any remaining parameter is appended to the adapter handle. In other words, the adaptation works
5618      * as follows:
5619      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5620      * T target(A...)
5621      * V filter(B... , T)
5622      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5623      *     T t = target(a...);
5624      *     return filter(b..., t);
5625      * }</pre></blockquote>
5626      * <p>
5627      * If the filter handle is a unary function, then this method behaves like {@link #filterReturnValue(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5628      *
5629      * @param target the target method handle
5630      * @param filter the filter method handle
5631      * @return the adapter method handle
5632      */
5633     /* package */ static MethodHandle collectReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
5634         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5635         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5636         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5637         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().collectReturnValueForm(filterType.basicType());
5638         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
5639         if (filterType.parameterList().size() > 1) {
5640             for (int i = 0 ; i < filterType.parameterList().size() - 1 ; i++) {
5641                 newType = newType.appendParameterTypes(filterType.parameterType(i));
5642             }
5643         }
5644         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5645         return result;
5646     }
5647 
5648     /**
5649      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5650      * some of its arguments, and then calling the target with
5651      * the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original
5652      * sequence of arguments.
5653      * <p>
5654      * The pre-processing is performed by {@code combiner}, a second method handle.
5655      * Of the arguments passed to the adapter, the first {@code N} arguments
5656      * are copied to the combiner, which is then called.
5657      * (Here, {@code N} is defined as the parameter count of the combiner.)
5658      * After this, control passes to the target, with any result
5659      * from the combiner inserted before the original {@code N} incoming
5660      * arguments.
5661      * <p>
5662      * If the combiner returns a value, the first parameter type of the target
5663      * must be identical with the return type of the combiner, and the next
5664      * {@code N} parameter types of the target must exactly match the parameters
5665      * of the combiner.
5666      * <p>
5667      * If the combiner has a void return, no result will be inserted,
5668      * and the first {@code N} parameter types of the target
5669      * must exactly match the parameters of the combiner.
5670      * <p>
5671      * The resulting adapter is the same type as the target, except that the
5672      * first parameter type is dropped,
5673      * if it corresponds to the result of the combiner.
5674      * <p>
5675      * (Note that {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments} can be used to remove any arguments
5676      * that either the combiner or the target does not wish to receive.
5677      * If some of the incoming arguments are destined only for the combiner,
5678      * consider using {@link MethodHandle#asCollector asCollector} instead, since those
5679      * arguments will not need to be live on the stack on entry to the
5680      * target.)
5681      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5682      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5683 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5684 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5685 ...
5686 MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5687   "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5688     .bindTo(System.out);
5689 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5690   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5691 assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5692 MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, trace);
5693 // also prints "boo":
5694 assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5695      * }</pre></blockquote>
5696      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5697      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5698      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5699      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5700      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5701      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5702      * position. {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values of the
5703      * {@code target} parameters and arguments that follow the folded parameters
5704      * and arguments.
5705      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5706      * // there are N arguments in A...
5707      * T target(V, A[N]..., B...);
5708      * V combiner(A...);
5709      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5710      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5711      *   return target(v, a..., b...);
5712      * }
5713      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5714      * T target2(A[N]..., B...);
5715      * void combiner2(A...);
5716      * T adapter2(A... a, B... b) {
5717      *   combiner2(a...);
5718      *   return target2(a..., b...);
5719      * }
5720      * }</pre></blockquote>
5721      * <p>
5722      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5723      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5724      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5725      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5726      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5727      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5728      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code combiner}'s return type
5729      *          is non-void and not the same as the first argument type of
5730      *          the target, or if the initial {@code N} argument types
5731      *          of the target
5732      *          (skipping one matching the {@code combiner}'s return type)
5733      *          are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}
5734      */
5735     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle combiner) {
5736         return foldArguments(target, 0, combiner);
5737     }
5738 
5739     /**
5740      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, starting at a given position, and then
5741      * calling the target with the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original sequence of arguments just
5742      * before the folded arguments.
5743      * <p>
5744      * This method is closely related to {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}, but allows to control the
5745      * position in the parameter list at which folding takes place. The argument controlling this, {@code pos}, is a
5746      * zero-based index. The aforementioned method {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)} assumes position
5747      * 0.
5748      *
5749      * @apiNote Example:
5750      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5751     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5752     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5753     ...
5754     MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5755     "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5756     .bindTo(System.out);
5757     MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5758     "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5759     assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5760     MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, 1, trace);
5761     // also prints "jum":
5762     assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5763      * }</pre></blockquote>
5764      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5765      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5766      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5767      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5768      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5769      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5770      * position. {@code Z}/{@code z} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types
5771      * and values of the {@code target} parameters and arguments that precede and
5772      * follow the folded parameters and arguments starting at {@code pos},
5773      * respectively.
5774      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5775      * // there are N arguments in A...
5776      * T target(Z..., V, A[N]..., B...);
5777      * V combiner(A...);
5778      * T adapter(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5779      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5780      *   return target(z..., v, a..., b...);
5781      * }
5782      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5783      * T target2(Z..., A[N]..., B...);
5784      * void combiner2(A...);
5785      * T adapter2(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5786      *   combiner2(a...);
5787      *   return target2(z..., a..., b...);
5788      * }
5789      * }</pre></blockquote>
5790      * <p>
5791      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5792      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5793      *
5794      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5795      * @param pos the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5796      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5797      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5798      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5799      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5800      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5801      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5802      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5803      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at position {@code pos} of the target signature (skipping one matching
5804      *              the {@code combiner}'s return type) are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5805      *
5806      * @see #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5807      * @since 9
5808      */
5809     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle combiner) {
5810         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5811         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5812         Class<?> rtype = foldArgumentChecks(pos, targetType, combinerType);
5813         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5814         boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5815         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + pos, dropResult, combinerType.basicType());
5816         MethodType newType = targetType;
5817         if (!dropResult) {
5818             newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos + 1);
5819         }
5820         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5821         return result;
5822     }
5823 
5824     private static Class<?> foldArgumentChecks(int foldPos, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType) {
5825         int foldArgs   = combinerType.parameterCount();
5826         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5827         int foldVals = rtype == void.class ? 0 : 1;
5828         int afterInsertPos = foldPos + foldVals;
5829         boolean ok = (targetType.parameterCount() >= afterInsertPos + foldArgs);
5830         if (ok) {
5831             for (int i = 0; i < foldArgs; i++) {
5832                 if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(i + afterInsertPos)) {
5833                     ok = false;
5834                     break;
5835                 }
5836             }
5837         }
5838         if (ok && foldVals != 0 && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(foldPos))
5839             ok = false;
5840         if (!ok)
5841             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5842         return rtype;
5843     }
5844 
5845     /**
5846      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, then calling the target with the result
5847      * of the pre-processing replacing the argument at the given position.
5848      *
5849      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5850      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5851      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5852      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5853      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5854      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5855      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5856      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5857      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is not the same as the argument type at position
5858      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5859      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature are
5860      *              not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5861      */
5862     /*non-public*/
5863     static MethodHandle filterArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5864         return argumentsWithCombiner(true, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5865     }
5866 
5867     /**
5868      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, calling the target with the result of
5869      * the pre-processing inserted into the original sequence of arguments at the given position.
5870      *
5871      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5872      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5873      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5874      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5875      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5876      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5877      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5878      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5879      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5880      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5881      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature
5882      *              (skipping {@code position} where the {@code combiner}'s return will be folded in) are not identical
5883      *              with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5884      */
5885     /*non-public*/
5886     static MethodHandle foldArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5887         return argumentsWithCombiner(false, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5888     }
5889 
5890     private static MethodHandle argumentsWithCombiner(boolean filter, MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5891         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5892         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5893         Class<?> rtype = argumentsWithCombinerChecks(position, filter, targetType, combinerType, argPositions);
5894         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5895 
5896         MethodType newType = targetType;
5897         LambdaForm lform;
5898         if (filter) {
5899             lform = result.editor().filterArgumentsForm(1 + position, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5900         } else {
5901             boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5902             lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + position, dropResult, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5903             if (!dropResult) {
5904                 newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(position, position + 1);
5905             }
5906         }
5907         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5908         return result;
5909     }
5910 
5911     private static Class<?> argumentsWithCombinerChecks(int position, boolean filter, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType, int ... argPos) {
5912         int combinerArgs = combinerType.parameterCount();
5913         if (argPos.length != combinerArgs) {
5914             throw newIllegalArgumentException("combiner and argument map must be equal size", combinerType, argPos.length);
5915         }
5916         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5917 
5918         for (int i = 0; i < combinerArgs; i++) {
5919             int arg = argPos[i];
5920             if (arg < 0 || arg > targetType.parameterCount()) {
5921                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("arg outside of target parameterRange", targetType, arg);
5922             }
5923             if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(arg)) {
5924                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("target argument type at position " + arg
5925                         + " must match combiner argument type at index " + i + ": " + targetType
5926                         + " -> " + combinerType + ", map: " + Arrays.toString(argPos));
5927             }
5928         }
5929         if (filter && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(position)) {
5930             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5931         }
5932         return rtype;
5933     }
5934 
5935     /**
5936      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5937      * by guarding it with a test, a boolean-valued method handle.
5938      * If the guard fails, a fallback handle is called instead.
5939      * All three method handles must have the same corresponding
5940      * argument and return types, except that the return type
5941      * of the test must be boolean, and the test is allowed
5942      * to have fewer arguments than the other two method handles.
5943      * <p>
5944      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5945      * represents the uniform result type of the three involved handles;
5946      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the {@code target}
5947      * parameters and arguments that are consumed by the {@code test}; and
5948      * {@code B}/{@code b}, those types and values of the {@code target}
5949      * parameters and arguments that are not consumed by the {@code test}.
5950      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5951      * boolean test(A...);
5952      * T target(A...,B...);
5953      * T fallback(A...,B...);
5954      * T adapter(A... a,B... b) {
5955      *   if (test(a...))
5956      *     return target(a..., b...);
5957      *   else
5958      *     return fallback(a..., b...);
5959      * }
5960      * }</pre></blockquote>
5961      * Note that the test arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5962      * be modified by execution of the test, and so are passed unchanged
5963      * from the caller to the target or fallback as appropriate.
5964      * @param test method handle used for test, must return boolean
5965      * @param target method handle to call if test passes
5966      * @param fallback method handle to call if test fails
5967      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified if/then/else logic
5968      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5969      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code test} does not return boolean,
5970      *          or if all three method types do not match (with the return
5971      *          type of {@code test} changed to match that of the target).
5972      */
5973     public static MethodHandle guardWithTest(MethodHandle test,
5974                                MethodHandle target,
5975                                MethodHandle fallback) {
5976         MethodType gtype = test.type();
5977         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5978         MethodType ftype = fallback.type();
5979         if (!ttype.equals(ftype))
5980             throw misMatchedTypes("target and fallback types", ttype, ftype);
5981         if (gtype.returnType() != boolean.class)
5982             throw newIllegalArgumentException("guard type is not a predicate "+gtype);
5983         List<Class<?>> targs = ttype.parameterList();
5984         test = dropArgumentsToMatch(test, 0, targs, 0, true);
5985         if (test == null) {
5986             throw misMatchedTypes("target and test types", ttype, gtype);
5987         }
5988         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithTest(test, target, fallback);
5989     }
5990 
5991     static <T> RuntimeException misMatchedTypes(String what, T t1, T t2) {
5992         return newIllegalArgumentException(what + " must match: " + t1 + " != " + t2);
5993     }
5994 
5995     /**
5996      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5997      * by running it inside an exception handler.
5998      * If the target returns normally, the adapter returns that value.
5999      * If an exception matching the specified type is thrown, the fallback
6000      * handle is called instead on the exception, plus the original arguments.
6001      * <p>
6002      * The target and handler must have the same corresponding
6003      * argument and return types, except that handler may omit trailing arguments
6004      * (similarly to the predicate in {@link #guardWithTest guardWithTest}).
6005      * Also, the handler must have an extra leading parameter of {@code exType} or a supertype.
6006      * <p>
6007      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
6008      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and {@code handler},
6009      * and correspondingly that of the resulting adapter; {@code A}/{@code a},
6010      * the types and values of arguments to the resulting handle consumed by
6011      * {@code handler}; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the
6012      * resulting handle discarded by {@code handler}.
6013      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6014      * T target(A..., B...);
6015      * T handler(ExType, A...);
6016      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
6017      *   try {
6018      *     return target(a..., b...);
6019      *   } catch (ExType ex) {
6020      *     return handler(ex, a...);
6021      *   }
6022      * }
6023      * }</pre></blockquote>
6024      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
6025      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
6026      * from the caller to the handler, if the handler is invoked.
6027      * <p>
6028      * The target and handler must return the same type, even if the handler
6029      * always throws.  (This might happen, for instance, because the handler
6030      * is simulating a {@code finally} clause).
6031      * To create such a throwing handler, compose the handler creation logic
6032      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
6033      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
6034      * @param target method handle to call
6035      * @param exType the type of exception which the handler will catch
6036      * @param handler method handle to call if a matching exception is thrown
6037      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified try/catch logic
6038      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
6039      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code handler} does not accept
6040      *          the given exception type, or if the method handle types do
6041      *          not match in their return types and their
6042      *          corresponding parameters
6043      * @see MethodHandles#tryFinally(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6044      */
6045     public static MethodHandle catchException(MethodHandle target,
6046                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
6047                                 MethodHandle handler) {
6048         MethodType ttype = target.type();
6049         MethodType htype = handler.type();
6050         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
6051             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
6052         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
6053             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
6054             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
6055         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
6056             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
6057         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
6058         if (handler == null) {
6059             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
6060         }
6061         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
6062     }
6063 
6064     /**
6065      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
6066      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
6067      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
6068      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
6069      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
6070      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
6071      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
6072      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
6073      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
6074      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
6075      */
6076     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
6077         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
6078             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
6079         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
6080     }
6081 
6082     /**
6083      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
6084      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
6085      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
6086      * <p>
6087      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
6088      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
6089      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
6090      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
6091      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
6092      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
6093      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
6094      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
6095      * </ul>
6096      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
6097      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
6098      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
6099      * <p>
6100      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
6101      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
6102      * <p>
6103      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
6104      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
6105      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
6106      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
