6107      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
6108      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
6109      * <p>
6110      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
6111      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
6112      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
6113      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
6114      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
6115      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
6116      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
6117      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
6118      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
6119      * <p>
6120      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
6121      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
6122      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
6123      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
6124      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
6125      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
6126      * <a id="astar"></a>
6127      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
6128      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
6129      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
6130      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
6131      * <p>
6132      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
6133      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
6134      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
6135      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
6136      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
6137      * <p>
6138      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
6139      * <a id="effid"></a>
6140      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
6141      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
6142      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
6143      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
6144      * that longest list.
6145      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
6146      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
6147      * <p>
6148      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
6149      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
6150      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
6151      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
6152      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
6153      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
6154      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
6155      * </ol>
6156      * <p>
6157      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
6158      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
6159      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
6160      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
6161      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
6162      * iteration variable type.
6163      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
6164      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
6165      * </ol>
6166      * <p>
6167      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
6168      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
6169      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
6170      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
6171      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
6172      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
6173      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
6174      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
6175      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
6176      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
6177      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
6178      * the "internal parameter list".
6179      * </ul>
6180      * <p>
6181      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
6182      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
6183      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
6184      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
6185      * type.
6186      * </ol>
6187      * <p>
6188      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
6189      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
6190      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
6191      * </ol>
6192      * <p>
6193      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
6194      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6195      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
6196      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
6197      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
6198      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
6199      * </ol>
6200      * <p>
6201      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
6202      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
6203      * type.
6204      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
6205      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
6206      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
6207      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
6208      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
6209      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
6210      * loop return type.
6211      * </ol>
6212      * <p>
6213      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
6214      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
6215      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
6216      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
6217      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
6218      * pad out the end of the list.
6219      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
6220      * </ol>
6221      * <p>
6222      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
6223      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
6224      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6225      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6226      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
6227      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
6228      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
6229      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
6230      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
6231      * </ol>
6232      * <p>
6233      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
6234      * <ul>
6235      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
6236      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
6237      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
6238      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
6239      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
6240      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
6241      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
6242      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
6243      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
6244      * </ul>
6245      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
6246      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
6247      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
6248      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
6249      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
6250      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
6251      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
6252      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
6253      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
6254      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
6255      * <p>
6256      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
6257      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
6258      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
6259      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
6260      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
6261      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
6262      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
6263      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
6264      * (in argument order).
6265      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
6266      * returns {@code false}.
6267      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
6268      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
6269      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
6270      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
6271      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
6272      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
6273      * except by throwing an exception.
6274      * </ol>
6275      * <p>
6276      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
6277      * <ul>
6278      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
6279      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
6280      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
6281      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
6282      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
6283      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
6284      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
6285      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
6286      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
6287      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
6288      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
6289      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
6290      * </ul>
6291      * <p>
6292      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
6293      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
6294      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
6295      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6296      * V... init...(A...);
6297      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
6298      * V... step...(V..., A...);
6299      * R fini...(V..., A...);
6300      * R loop(A... a) {
6301      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
6302      *   for (;;) {
6303      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
6304      *       v = s(v..., a...);
6305      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
6306      *         return f(v..., a...);
6307      *       }
6308      *     }
6309      *   }
6310      * }
6311      * }</pre></blockquote>
6312      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
6313      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
6314      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
6315      *
6316      * @apiNote Example:
6317      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6318      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6319      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
6320      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
6321      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
6322      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
6323      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
6324      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6325      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6326      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6327      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6328      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6329      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
6330      * }</pre></blockquote>
6331      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
6332      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6333      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6334      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
6335      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
6336      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
6337      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
6338      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6339      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6340      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
6341      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
6342      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6343      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6344      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6345      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
6346      * }</pre></blockquote>
6347      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
6348      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6349      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6350      * static class FacLoop {
6351      *   final int k;
6352      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
6353      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
6354      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
6355      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
6356      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
6357      * }
6358      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
6359      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6360      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6361      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6362      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
6363      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6364      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6365      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6366      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
6367      * }</pre></blockquote>
6368      *
6369      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
6370      *
6371      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
6372      *
6373      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
6374      *
6375      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6376      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6377      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6378      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6379      * @since 9
6380      */
6381     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
6382         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
6383         loopChecks0(clauses);
6384 
6385         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
6386         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
6387         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
6388         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
6389 
6390         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
6391             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
6392             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
6393             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
6394             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
6395         });
6396 
6397         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
6398         final int nclauses = init.size();
6399 
6400         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
6401         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
6402         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6403             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
6404             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
6405             if (in == null && st == null) {
6406                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
6407             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
6408                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
6409                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
6410             } else {
6411                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
6412             }
6413         }
6414         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
6415                 collect(Collectors.toList());
6416 
6417         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
6418         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
6419         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
6420 
6421         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
6422         // Step 1D: check other types.
6423         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
6424         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
6425                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
6426         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
6427         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
6428 
6429         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
6430         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
6431         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
6432         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
6433 
6434         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
6435         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6436             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
6437             if (init.get(i) == null) {
6438                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
6439             }
6440             if (step.get(i) == null) {
6441                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
6442             }
6443             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
6444                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
6445             }
6446             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
6447                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
6448             }
6449         }
6450 
6451         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
6452         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
6453         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
6454         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
6455         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
6456         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
6457 
6458         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6459                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
6460         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6461                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
6462 
6463         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
6464     }
6465 
6466     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
6467         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
6468             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
6469         }
6470         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
6471             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
6472         }
6473         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
6474             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
6475         }
6476     }
6477 
6478     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
6479         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
6480             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
6481                     st.type().returnType());
6482         }
6483     }
6484 
6485     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
6486         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6487         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
6488                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
6489                         map(MethodHandle::type).
6490                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
6491                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
6492                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6493         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
6494     }
6495 
6496     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
6497         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6498         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6499     }
6500 
6501     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
6502         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
6503         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
6504         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
6505     }
6506 
6507     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
6508         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6509                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
6510             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
6511                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
6512         }
6513     }
6514 
6515     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
6516         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6517                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
6518             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
6519                     loopReturnType + ")");
6520         }
6521 
6522         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
6523             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
6524         }
6525         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6526                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
6527             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
6528         }
6529     }
6530 
6531     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
6532         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6533                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
6534             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
6535                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
6536         }
6537     }
6538 
6539     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
6540         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
6541             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
6542             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
6543             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
6544         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
6545     }
6546 
6547     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
6548         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
6549     }
6550 
6551     /**
6552      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6553      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6554      * <p>
6555      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6556      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
6557      * evaluates to {@code true}).
6558      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
6559      * <p>
6560      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6561      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6562      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6563      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6564      * <p>
6565      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6566      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6567      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6568      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6569      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6570      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6571      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6572      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6573      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6574      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6575      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6576      * additional state variable of the loop.
6577      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6578      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6579      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6580      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6581      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6582      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6583      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6584      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6585      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6586      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6587      * </ul>
6588      * <p>
6589      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6590      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6591      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6592      * from the external parameter list.
6593      * </ul>
6594      * <p>
6595      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6596      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6597      * passed to the loop.
6598      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6599      * V init(A...);
6600      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6601      * V body(V, A...);
6602      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
6603      *   V v = init(a...);
6604      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
6605      *     v = body(v, a...);
6606      *   }
6607      *   return v;
6608      * }
6609      * }</pre></blockquote>
6610      *
6611      * @apiNote Example:
6612      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6613      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
6614      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6615      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
6616      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
6617      *   zip.add(a.next());
6618      *   zip.add(b.next());
6619      *   return zip;
6620      * }
6621      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
6622      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
6623      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
6624      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
6625      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
6626      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
6627      * }</pre></blockquote>
6628      *
6629      *
6630      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6631      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6632      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6633      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6634      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6635      *     MethodHandle[]
6636      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
6637      *         varBody   = { init, body };
6638      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6639      * }
6640      * }</pre></blockquote>
6641      *
6642      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6643      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6644      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6645      *             above for other constraints.
6646      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6647      *             See above for other constraints.
6648      *
6649      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6650      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6651      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6652      *
6653      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6654      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6655      * @since 9
6656      */
6657     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6658         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6659         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6660         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
6661         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
6662         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6663     }
6664 
6665     /**
6666      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6667      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6668      * <p>
6669      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6670      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
6671      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
6672      * <p>
6673      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6674      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6675      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6676      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6677      * <p>
6678      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6679      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6680      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6681      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6682      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6683      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6684      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6685      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6686      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6687      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6688      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6689      * additional state variable of the loop.
6690      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6691      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6692      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6693      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6694      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6695      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6696      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6697      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6698      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6699      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6700      * </ul>
6701      * <p>
6702      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6703      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6704      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6705      * from the external parameter list.
6706      * </ul>
6707      * <p>
6708      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6709      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6710      * passed to the loop.
6711      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6712      * V init(A...);
6713      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6714      * V body(V, A...);
6715      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6716      *   V v = init(a...);
6717      *   do {
6718      *     v = body(v, a...);
6719      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6720      *   return v;
6721      * }
6722      * }</pre></blockquote>
6723      *
6724      * @apiNote Example:
6725      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6726      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6727      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6728      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6729      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6730      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6731      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6732      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6733      * }</pre></blockquote>
6734      *
6735      *
6736      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6737      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6738      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6739      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6740      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6741      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6742      *     return loop(clause);
6743      * }
6744      * }</pre></blockquote>
6745      *
6746      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6747      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6748      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6749      *             See above for other constraints.
6750      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6751      *             above for other constraints.
6752      *
6753      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6754      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6755      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6756      *
6757      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6758      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6759      * @since 9
6760      */
6761     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6762         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6763         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6764         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6765         return loop(clause);
6766     }
6767 
6768     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6769         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6770         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6771         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6772         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6773         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6774         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6775         if (returnType == void.class) {
6776             // OK
6777         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6778             // leading V argument missing => error
6779             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6780             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6781         } else {
6782             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6783         }
6784         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6785         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6786                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6787             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6788         }
6789         if (init != null) {
6790             MethodType initType = init.type();
6791             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6792                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6793                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6794             }
6795         }
6796     }
6797 
6798     /**
6799      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6800      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6801      * <p>
6802      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6803      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6804      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6805      * <p>
6806      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6807      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6808      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6809      * <p>
6810      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6811      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6812      * iteration variable.
6813      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6814      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6815      * <p>
6816      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6817      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6818      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6819      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6820      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6821      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6822      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6823      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6824      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6825      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6826      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6827      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6828      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6829      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6830      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6831      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6832      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6833      * additional state variable of the loop.
6834      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6835      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6836      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6837      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6838      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6839      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6840      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6841      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6842      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6843      * </ul>
6844      * <p>
6845      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6846      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6847      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6848      * from the external parameter list.
6849      * </ul>
6850      * <p>
6851      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6852      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6853      * arguments passed to the loop.
6854      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6855      * int iterations(A...);
6856      * V init(A...);
6857      * V body(V, int, A...);
6858      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6859      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6860      *   V v = init(a...);
6861      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6862      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6863      *   }
6864      *   return v;
6865      * }
6866      * }</pre></blockquote>
6867      *
6868      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6869      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6870      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6871      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6872      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6873      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6874      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6875      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6876      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6877      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6878      * }</pre></blockquote>
6879      *
6880      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6881      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6882      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6883      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6884      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6885      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6886      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6887      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6888      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6889      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6890      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6891      * }</pre></blockquote>
6892      *
6893      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6894      * as loop parameters:
6895      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6896      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6897      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6898      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6899      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6900      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6901      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6902      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6903      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6904      * }</pre></blockquote>
6905      *
6906      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6907      * to enforce a loop type:
6908      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6909      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6910      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6911      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6912      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6913      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6914      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6915      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6916      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6917      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6918      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6919      * }</pre></blockquote>
6920      *
6921      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6922      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6923      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6924      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6925      * }
6926      * }</pre></blockquote>
6927      *
6928      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6929      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6930      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6931      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6932      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6933      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6934      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6935      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6936      *             See above for other constraints.
6937      *
6938      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6939      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6940      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6941      *
6942      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6943      * @since 9
6944      */
6945     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6946         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6947     }
6948 
6949     /**
6950      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6951      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6952      * <p>
6953      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6954      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6955      * values of the loop counter.
6956      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6957      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6958      * <p>
6959      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6960      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6961      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6962      * <p>
6963      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6964      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6965      * iteration variable.
6966      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6967      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6968      * <p>
6969      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6970      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6971      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6972      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6973      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6974      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6975      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6976      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6977      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6978      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6979      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6980      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6981      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6982      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6983      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6984      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6985      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6986      * additional state variable of the loop.
6987      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6988      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6989      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6990      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6991      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6992      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6993      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6994      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6995      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6996      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
6997      * to the external parameter list.
6998      * </ul>
6999      * <p>
7000      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
7001      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
7002      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
7003      * from the external parameter list.
7004      * </ul>
7005      * <p>
7006      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
7007      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
7008      * arguments passed to the loop.
7009      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7010      * int start(A...);
7011      * int end(A...);
7012      * V init(A...);
7013      * V body(V, int, A...);
7014      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
7015      *   int e = end(a...);
7016      *   int s = start(a...);
7017      *   V v = init(a...);
7018      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
7019      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
7020      *   }
7021      *   return v;
7022      * }
7023      * }</pre></blockquote>
7024      *
7025      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
7026      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7027      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7028      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
7029      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
7030      *     // the following semantics:
7031      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
7032      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
7033      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
7034      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7035      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
7036      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
7037      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
7038      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
7039      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
7040      *     }
7041      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
7042      *     MethodHandle[]
7043      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
7044      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
7045      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
7046      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
7047      * }
7048      * }</pre></blockquote>
7049      *
7050      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
7051      *              See above for other constraints.
7052      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
7053      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
7054      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7055      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7056      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7057      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7058      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
7059      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7060      *             See above for other constraints.
7061      *
7062      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
7063      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
7064      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
7065      *
7066      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
7067      * @since 9
7068      */
7069     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7070         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
7071         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
7072         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
7073         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
7074         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
7075         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
7076         MethodHandle retv = null;
7077         if (returnType != void.class) {
7078             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
7079             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
7080             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
7081         }
7082         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
7083         MethodHandle[]
7084             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
7085             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
7086             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
7087         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
7088     }
7089 
7090     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7091         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
7092         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
7093         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7094         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
7095         if (counterType != int.class) {
7096             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
7097             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
7098         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
7099             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
7100             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
7101         }
7102         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7103         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7104         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
7105         // strip leading V value if present
7106         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7107         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7108             // argument list has no "V" => error
7109             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7110             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7111         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
7112             // missing I type => error
7113             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
7114             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7115         }
7116         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
7117         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
7118             // special case; take lists from end handle
7119             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
7120             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
7121         }
7122         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
7123         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7124             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
7125         }
7126         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
7127             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7128             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
7129         }
7130         if (init != null) {
7131             MethodType initType = init.type();
7132             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7133                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7134                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
7135             }
7136         }
7137     }
7138 
7139     /**
7140      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
7141      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
7142      * <p>
7143      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
7144      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
7145      * <p>
7146      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
7147      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
7148      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
7149      * <p>
7150      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
7151      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
7152      * iteration variable.
7153      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
7154      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
7155      * <p>
7156      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
7157      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
7158      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
7159      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
7160      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
7161      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
7162      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
7163      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
7164      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
7165      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
7166      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
7167      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
7168      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
7169      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
7170      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
7171      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
7172      * additional state variable of the loop.
7173      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
7174      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
7175      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
7176      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
7177      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7178      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
7179      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
7180      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
7181      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
7182      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
7183      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
7184      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
7185      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7186      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
7187      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
7188      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
7189      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
7190      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7191      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
7192      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
7193      * </ul>
7194      * <p>
7195      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
7196      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
7197      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
7198      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7199      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
7200      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
7201      * <p>
7202      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
7203      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
7204      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
7205      * from the external parameter list.
7206      * </ul>
7207      * <p>
7208      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
7209      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
7210      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
7211      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7212      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
7213      * V init(A...);
7214      * V body(V,T,A...);
7215      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
7216      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
7217      *   V v = init(a...);
7218      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
7219      *     T t = it.next();
7220      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
7221      *   }
7222      *   return v;
7223      * }
7224      * }</pre></blockquote>
7225      *
7226      * @apiNote Example:
7227      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7228      * // get an iterator from a list
7229      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
7230      *   r.add(0, e);
7231      *   return r;
7232      * }
7233      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
7234      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
7235      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
7236      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
7237      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
7238      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
7239      * }</pre></blockquote>
7240      *
7241      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
7242      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7243      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7244      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
7245      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7246      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7247      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
7248      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
7249      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
7250      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7251      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7252      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7253      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7254      *     }
7255      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
7256      *     MethodHandle[]
7257      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
7258      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
7259      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7260      * }
7261      * }</pre></blockquote>
7262      *
7263      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
7264      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
7265      *                 See above for other constraints.
7266      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7267      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7268      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7269      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7270      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
7271      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7272      *             See above for other constraints.
7273      *
7274      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
7275      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
7276      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
7277      *
7278      * @since 9
7279      */
7280     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7281         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
7282         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7283         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
7284         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
7285         MethodHandle startIter;
7286         MethodHandle nextVal;
7287         {
7288             MethodType iteratorType;
7289             if (iterator == null) {
7290                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
7291                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
7292                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
7293             } else {
7294                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
7295                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
7296                 startIter = iterator;
7297             }
